Another Report on the Fushun Massacre 51

Zhang Rongjiu's Story of Escaping from Death

More Than Three Thousand People Killed by a Single Bullet

Tragic Voices Heard After the Massacre

Returning Covered in Blood, Still Suspecting It Was a Ghost

Beiping Correspondence: The Fushun Pingdingshan Japanese Army Massacre incident has been reported in previous newspapers by the American International News Agency reporter, Mr. Hunter, after inspecting and publishing a report. Now, Zhang Rongjiu, a Fushun refugee, escaped to Beiping yesterday, detailing the situation of the Japanese army's atrocities at the time. Zhang is from Lizigou. At that time, his family was tricked into going to Pingdingshan, and all his family members were killed. He himself was able to survive because he was covered in blood. After the incident, he escaped and came to Beiping. He was still horrified when he spoke. After finishing, he also said that if there was half a word of lie, he would be punished by heaven, which shows his grief and anger. The details of his conversation are recorded as follows:

"I am from Lizigou, Fushun County. On the morning of September 16, a team of Japanese soldiers suddenly came to our village, led by a translator who could speak Chinese. They told each household that the Japanese army wanted to borrow our village to practice combat, and told us residents to all hide in the nearby Pingdingshan mountain ditch. At that time, my family of six, my mother, wife, son, my brother Pengjiu, and my sister-in-law Zhao, were eating. We were about to tell him to wait until we finished eating before leaving, but those fierce Japanese soldiers, one by one, glared their eyes, holding their guns and saying, 'Go, go.' We didn't bother to pack up the eating utensils and ran out in a very embarrassing manner. When we got to the entrance of the village, we saw that all the people in the village, one by one, supporting the old and carrying the young, were heading towards Pingdingshan under the escort of a team of Japanese soldiers. When we got to Pingdingshan, we saw that the people from Pingdingshan Village were already sitting there in groups of three or five. Some said that the Japanese army was going to practice artillery, and some said that the Xuantong Emperor had sent an imperial envoy to distribute relief. But while they were discussing, six or seven hundred more farmers came, some women carrying babies, some old ladies in their seventies or eighties being supported, and they were also escorted by Japanese soldiers to this Pingdingshan ditch. It turned out that these were the people from Qianjinbao. Among them was a distant relative of mine, called Tong Erge, who was carrying his mother on his back. I greeted him and told him to sit with me. Suddenly, I heard a whistle, and I saw that the Japanese soldiers who had escorted us and the Japanese soldiers who had escorted other villagers gathered together. After another round of commands, they separated around us. The few people who could speak Chinese said to us, 'Now the emperor is going to give you money. You all kneel down and thank him. Let us take a picture first, and then you can receive the reward.' As they spoke, the Japanese soldiers were busy arranging things that looked like cylindrical black and shiny things on many tripods. We thought they were cameras, but we saw a few people in our village standing up and running, shouting, 'It's not good, the Japanese are going to fire machine guns.' Before they finished speaking, we saw that the long筒-shaped cameras we imagined were spitting out flames with a ping ping pang pang sound. At that time, more than three thousand people were running around, calling for help, shouting for their children and daughters in great chaos, and everyone fell down in response. My brother was more alert than me. He was the first to stand up and try to escape, but the ruthless bullet hit him right in the head. A stream of blood shot out from his forehead and he fell down, just lying on top of me. I also fell down on the ground with him. After a period of ghosts crying and gods howling, the earth-shattering chaos passed. Then, I heard the faint humming, moaning, and wailing sounds coming from all around. Then, I heard the Japanese soldiers laughing, scolding, cursing, the sound of bayonets being used, screams of panic, tragic sounds, and fading sounds. While I was panicked, and being pressed down by my brother's body, and scared to move, half-conscious, I felt the Japanese soldiers kicking me twice with their leather shoes. But my whole body was soaked in my brother's blood, dripping with blood. The Japanese soldiers thought I was definitely dead. After I don't know how much time passed, I heard no sound around me, and the sky seemed to be dim. I peeked and saw corpses all around, some lying on their backs, some falling face down, and the ground was full of crimson blood. I barely struggled to get up and looked around. There was not a single living person. My mother, my wife, my sister-in-law, my brother, each of them had been dead for a long time, and the wounds were still bleeding. My son died even more tragically, his face blurred and his brains splattered. After this tragic change, I was like a madman, like a fool, and I didn't know whether I was a human or a ghost, whether I was dead or alive. I tried my best to run wildly, wanting to run back to the village, but looking from afar, the raging fire in our village had not yet been extinguished. At this time, my mind had become slightly clearer. I suddenly remembered that there was a relative in Gongjiagou across the river. I crawled and rolled to that place. When the relative saw me looking like a blood ghost, he was trembling with fear. He put me in the house and gave me a bowl of cold water to drink. It took me a long time to speak. The next day, he was afraid that the Japanese soldiers would find me and implicate his family. He changed me into a set of old clothes, gathered some travel money, and sent me to another relative inside the customs. I think I was frightened. I often woke up in my sleep at night and ran wildly, or screamed. My family is all dead, and I don't want to live anymore. Alas, this is the happiness enjoyed by the citizens of "Manchukuo." This is the taste that countless people in the Northeast taste every day. What I have said above is my personal experience of Zhang Rongjiu escaping from death. If there is half a word of lie, I will be punished by heaven." (22nd)

Japanese Atrocities 52

｜Northeast People Rise Up in Struggle｜

Although the people of Northeast China harbored resentment towards Japan, before September 18th, it wasn't very intense. Even after September 18th, it hadn't truly become a matter of sworn enemies. Therefore, when the "Manchukuo Puppet State" was established, there were still many people who put on a show of support. Some of them were, of course, forcing a smile through tears and reluctantly complying to endure the situation temporarily. Some genuinely welcomed the restoration of the Qing Dynasty, especially in culturally backward areas, where they felt that the appearance of the true emperor was a future blessing. However, after several months, not only did their dreams not come true, but those who initially thought it was a bitter affair naturally felt even more that there was nowhere to shed their tears. Of course, they were absolutely not allowed to speak (if three people talked, it would easily be a crime). Even those who originally supported the puppet regime's emergence felt unable to express their suffering. They were constantly scolded. Those who held official positions within the puppet government could only wash their faces with tears in private. Ordinary merchants and farmers also found their food tasteless and their sleep restless. The reasons for their unease were: first, the number of Japanese officials increased day by day (it is said that all the unemployed intellectuals and vagrants in Japan envied the glory of holding official positions in Manchuria and came to Manchuria to become officials), and their power also grew day by day; second, Korean farmers streamed into the Northeast to cultivate land, even driving out the original landowners and forcing the original landlords and tenants to relocate, allowing them to reside and cultivate the land. As a result, people with land lost their land and became unemployed, and those who originally did odd jobs had no choice but to become beggars. Therefore, the Northeast people's resentment towards the Japanese has shifted from a few to a majority. People of all social classes almost universally hate the Japanese. This is no longer a simple landlord-tenant relationship but a widespread expansion of national hatred. The people of our three eastern provinces have mostly gained a new understanding, especially regarding relations with Japan. Although the time for a true reckoning has not yet arrived, there will eventually be a day to settle accounts with them.

Currently, the large-scale volunteer armies have undoubtedly failed. For example, Commander Su Bingwen, Generals Zhang Dianjiu, and Wu Delin raised the flag of resistance for two months, struggling to survive in the freezing snow. Bullets were being used up one by one, and food was being consumed day by day. Moreover, Japanese soldiers were continuously increasing their numbers. At the same time, the flanking attacks by the invaders, crossing the Greater Khingan Range from the Solon area to the north to strike Hailar from the side, made it impossible for the starving and freezing volunteer army to resist. However, although they failed, the Northeast people have awakened since then, and their anti-Japanese sentiment has increased even more due to the defeat. Even though Commander Su and his subordinates left the Northeast, the Northeast people did not sell themselves out, at least not in their hearts. Only a very small minority were willing to be lackeys of Japanese imperialism.

Therefore, Japan, which considers itself a conqueror, is also very wary of the activities of the volunteer army. According to the Japanese, the number of volunteer soldiers in August and September this year was no less than 250,000. According to our calculations, it was around 300,000. However, now that the "green curtain" [crops that can hide soldiers] has disappeared, the large-scale volunteer army has had to break into smaller units and temporarily lie low to wait for the coming year. However, at present, the combined number of volunteer armies that continue to operate and constantly attack the enemy is still no less than 100,000. The reason for not being able to win is that our army is relatively scattered, its organizational strength is not very solid, and it lacks guns, bullets, food, and clothing. The tactic of each person fighting on their own is too outdated. However, the so-called "Peace Preservation Guerrilla Force," which harasses the countryside and extorts and oppresses the people everywhere, is in fact a "Aggression Guerrilla Force," because when they come, the people cannot sleep peacefully. Everyone has no choice. In various counties in Liaoning, there are organizations of the Big Sword Society. On the 15th of this month, a large unit of the so-called "Peace Preservation Force" ran to Tuchengzi, west of Dashiqiao (a major station on the South Manchuria Railway), to fight guerrillas and engaged in a battle with the local Big Sword Society. They killed their commander, Colonel Mori, and Lieutenant Kinoshita on the spot. In addition, Majors Nagata and Abe, and Chief Quartermaster Takahashi, and other important officers, were all seriously injured. Now, the Japanese side is mobilizing a large force, preparing to carry out their old trick of massacre.

X X X X

Since the Japanese army invaded Northeast China and established the puppet state, not only are Japanese officials in Changchun flaunting the "Manchukuo" signboard and acting recklessly, but also in the county governments, newly established positions of councilors, secretaries, instructors, and patrol officers in the police stations are all filled by Japanese. Two or three months ago, a large number of Japanese ronin ran to Manchuria to become officials. Those who had special relationships with the military or the likes of Komai and Ohashi could become high-ranking officials; otherwise, they could also become small officials to satisfy their ambitions. In short, under the control of the great military power, the Japanese truly rose like dogs and chickens to heaven. High-ranking officials naturally controlled the entire "Manchukuo," exploiting it as much as possible, while small officials in the counties were even more direct extortionists. Their oppression of the common people was dozens or hundreds of times worse than that of the officials in the previous Qing Dynasty. This is because the officials in the previous Qing Dynasty were mostly crude, and their methods of extortion were also very clumsy, so poor people could still find a way to survive amidst the crudeness and clumsiness. But now the Japanese have learned many new methods of extortion, which are as dense as hairs on an ox. Their ways of making money are also bloodless. For example, the tobacco monopoly seems to have some justification, but the demands of the population census truly cause unrest even among chickens and dogs. All the interests of the people are taken away by them, even the fields (that have been cultivated) are arbitrarily occupied, leaving the farmers who till the land with nowhere to escape. Therefore, the Northeast people's resentment towards the Japanese increases day by day. All Japanese officials and Japanese dogs who go to the countryside arouse the resentment of the local people. Therefore, last month, the councilor of Fenghuang City, Tomota Toshiaki, the secretary, Nishi Tatsuki, the instructor, Shirai Narumi, and the patrol officers, Fujii and Kamon, were ostensibly sent by the Japanese military to persuade the volunteer army to surrender, but in fact, they went to the countryside to plunder. Any law-abiding commoner, as long as their family had some money, would be labeled as a "bandit" to extort money and fill their own pockets. Little did they know that they would happen to encounter the volunteer army led by Deng Tiemei, giving them a hard blow. The five "money-loving and greedy" fellows all lost their lives. Now, Japan has sent a regiment of infantry, attached with artillery, aircraft, and cavalry, which is confronting Deng's approximately 4,000 troops in the Motianling area east of Gaiping. In the near future, a bloody battle will be inevitable. (December 17th, in Shenyang)

He Chengjun to Go to Shaanxi to Supervise Troops 53

Chiang Orders Tian Songyao to Increase Troops in Northern Sichuan to Prevent Bandits from Roving

Banditry in Southern Hubei Intensifies Again, Zhu Shaoliang Orders General Offensive

Hankou Correspondence: Xu Xiangqian's remnants, after fleeing to Hanzhong, were blocked by the Shaanxi army and retreated south. After He Long's bandits dispersed, they had already fled to the border of Shaanxi and Sichuan. With their strength divided, it is easy to eliminate them. He Chengjun returned to Hankou from Nanjing a few days ago and planned to go to Xi'an soon to supervise the suppression. However, due to his poor health, he could not travel, so he could not make the trip. Now, because the task is important and should not be delayed, he has decided to depart from Hankou on the 25th. The personnel accompanying him to Shaanxi have already been appointed today (the 23rd). They include Chief of Staff Guan Linshu, Senior Staff Officer Xu Chengxi, Director of the Office Chen Guangzu, Adjutant Cao Zhenwu, Secretary Li Peng, Staff Officers Xu Xuzhong, Guan Wenhui, Wang Shuxian, Chen Yucang, Chief of the Military Supplies Section Fu Benhou, Section Member Ma Zhicheng, Chief of the Public Relations Section Peng Shuyou, Adjutants Zhao Yixue and Wang Xiongfei, Telegraph Operators Pan Tingzhen, Zhang Mingzhai, Liu Jiahua, and Che Zhaoyi, and Clerks Wang Boyin and Zhou Jisheng, totaling more than 20 people. After He's deployment, he immediately ordered the Pinghan Railway Bureau to prepare a special train and keep the fires lit. According to what He told the press, he will set up his headquarters in Xi'an for this trip to supervise the suppression of the remaining bandits and will be able to return to Hankou in at most one month. After He goes to Shaanxi, the affairs of the Pacification Headquarters will be handled by Chief of Staff Yang Kui on his behalf. As for the reserve team accompanying He to Shaanxi, the 1233rd Regiment, a supplement to the 44th Division, received He's order on the 22nd to take two trains to Zhengzhou and then to Xi'an. One battalion of infantry and one platoon of special service troops will be stationed in Huayuantun to escort He when he passes by. In addition, the 29th Army of Sichuan, under Tian Songyao, received a telegram from Chairman Chiang on the 17th, ordering them to increase their defense in northern Sichuan to prevent the remaining bandits from fleeing into Sichuan. He has sent Liu Hanxiong with three regiments to garrison in Guangyuan, and Li Weirui with four regiments to garrison in Tongjiang and Nanjiang. Together with the brigade previously dispatched and a brigade of border defense troops from Sichuan and Shaanxi, there are a total of two brigades and seven regiments. Although the bandits are fierce, they dare not easily enter this shady place.

The Kong bandits in southern Hubei have recently become rampant again. On the 14th, with a fake 7th, 8th, and 9th regiment, numbering several thousand, with more than 3,000 guns, they launched a surprise attack on Maojiapu in Lingma Township near Jinniu in Echeng County. The area only had four platoons from the first and third companies of the local militia, and their strength was weak. They were eventually defeated by the bandits. Two platoon leaders of the first company and more than 20 soldiers were killed in action, and more than 20 guns were lost. The commander of the third company was captured, along with 20 squad leaders, and 20 guns were lost. The bandits then occupied Maojiapu as a temporary nest. At the same time, there were bandit disturbances in other places. Zhu Shaoliang, the commander-in-chief of the bandit suppression in the border area of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, returned to Puqi from Changsha on an armored train on the 20th. On the 22nd, he ordered Guo Runao, Rong Jingfang, Xie Bin, Li Dingwu, and Zhang Gang to launch a general offensive against the bandits. Zhu was stationed on the armored train, personally directing the operation. On the 23rd, he sent his adjutant Li Dingmin to Hankou to report the progress of the suppression to the General Headquarters and the Pacification Headquarters. It is said that Zhu will go to northern Jiangxi to supervise the suppression after the remaining bandits there are eliminated. The General Headquarters may be moved to Jiujiang. (December 23rd)

Miserable and Terrifying Guanzhong 54

Xu and He's Two Factions Occupy the Southern Mountains

Student Unrest Occurs, All Schools Dissolved

Local Officials Only Know How to Demand Money

People's Livelihood Declines, Selling Wives and Children

The Cock's Crow at Dusk Is Universally Considered Ominous

Taiyuan Correspondence: Since the Xinhai Revolution in Shaanxi, the ravages of soldiers and bandits and the cruelty of natural disasters over the past 20 years have been extremely tragic. In particular, the two "tigers guarding the city" and the two major famines have caused immense suffering to the people and devastation to the region, which is most lamentable. Recently, a friend arrived in Taiyuan from Chang'an, describing the recent situation in Shaanxi in great detail. The disasters in Shaanxi are still as they were in the past. According to reports, remnants of the Communist Party, due to the disasters in Hubei and Henan provinces, have entered Shaanxi again. They were originally divided into two routes, one led by Xu Xiangqian, who is from Wutai, Shanxi, and a graduate of the Whampoa Military Academy, and the other led by He Long. Xu's troops entered Shaanxi from Laohekou, passing through Shangnan and Lantian, exiting the Ziwu Valley, and heading towards Hu, Feng, Qi, and Baoji, entering the Southern Mountains and Foping, plotting to occupy Hanzhong. He's troops followed the Han River around Baihe, attempting to flee into the Xing'an area. The northward flight of these two groups is similar to the White Wolf's actions in the early years of the Republic. Upon receiving the report, the central government initially ordered the Shaanxi army to suppress them. Later, seeing the situation was serious, they ordered He Chengjun to supervise the troops and coordinate with Yang Hucheng, the chairman of the Shaanxi provincial government, to block and suppress them. Currently, the anti-Communist troops entering Shaanxi include Liu Maoen, Xiao Zhichu, Hu Zongnan, and Huang Jie's troops, totaling four divisions. Aside from Sun Weiru in Gansu and Ma Qingyuan's troops, which have been disbanded due to suspicion, only Feng Qinzai and Wu Mianzhi's troops remain in Shaanxi under Yang Hucheng. Currently, Huang Jie's troops (Huang's troops were reorganized from the remnants of Fan Zhongxiu, Cui Erdan, and his own troops) and Feng Qinzai's troops are responsible for the defense of the Tongguan to Weinan area. Liu's troops are cooperating with Wu's troops, pursuing and suppressing from Shangluo all the way to Zhouzhi, where they are stationed. Xiao's troops are stationed in Hu County, and Hu's troops are stationed between Zhouzhi and Hu County. Wu Mianzhi's other troops are also stationed nearby. This is the current situation of the anti-bandit troops' deployment and the areas they are responsible for encircling. When the Communist Party first fled into Shaanxi, their numbers were no less than 50,000 to 60,000. After being blocked and suppressed by the government troops from all directions, the number of casualties and those who fled was not small. Moreover, the Communist Party was under pressure from both the front and the rear, and they were extremely exhausted upon entering Shaanxi. Some fell asleep while eating, and some fell asleep while standing. Their clothing was also mixed and messy, with men wearing women's clothes and women wearing men's clothes, because everything was looted from the people, so they didn't have time to distinguish them. When He's troops fled to Baihe, the troops of Zhang Feisheng's division made every effort to block them. The fierce fighting was extremely intense, with countless people killed. Baihe turned into a sea of blood, and its cruelty was unprecedented. Now, Xu and He each lead remnants into the Southern Mountains, relying on the mountains to occupy the area. After many fierce battles between the government troops and the Communist bandits, they have gained experience. They are taking a cautious attitude and are not easily engaging with the bandits. They are only sitting and watching the situation, waiting for an opportunity to change. Therefore, although the Communist Party in the Southern Mountains is said to be remnants, it will not be easy to eliminate them all at once. There is a rumor that the Communist Party's plan to flee into Shaanxi is to go from Shaanxi to Gansu to Mongolia, hoping to connect with Russia and communicate with each other. This is probably just the bandits exaggerating their strength. With their remaining troops, they probably do not have this power. However, the people of Shaanxi are eagerly hoping that the central government will eliminate these bandits as soon as possible.

A student movement occurred in Shaanxi a few days ago. It is said that it was incited by members of the Communist Party. However, the military and political authorities in the province immediately took swift action, arresting those who should be arrested and expelling those who should be expelled, responding severely and dissolving all schools above the middle school level. In order to protect themselves, people in all circles in the province often act like silent golden statues. Therefore, it is simply difficult to distinguish between Communist and non-Communist. In conversations, if one makes a slight slip of the tongue, they are either labeled as Communist or as a reactionary element. Living as one of those two carries extreme danger. Therefore, those who know how to protect themselves dare not comment on current affairs. As for the social economy, it is extremely depressed. The land is barren for thousands of miles, and farmers and workers are unemployed. The local officials are mostly military men. The tax collectors are illiterate, do not ask about people's livelihood, and only want silver dollars. One leaves and another comes, but they are all the same. Therefore, the people are unbearably oppressed. Some are dismantling their houses and selling them piecemeal, and some are posting their land deeds outside their doors and scattering them in all directions, each fleeing to save their lives. As for selling wives and children, it is indeed a common occurrence. However, even if one calls someone else "father," they will not care. If they themselves have no way to make a living, who would buy wives and children, inviting trouble for themselves? Shaanxi people are in this tragic and terrifying environment, and their future is dark. It is unknown when they will be able to see a glimmer of dawn.

Even more strange is that, in terms of heavenly and human affairs, there have been two recent events: (1) In the vicinity of Chang'an, within two or three hundred li, there has been a drought. The wells in all villages and communities have been reported to be dry. Every one or two days, the water drawn becomes mud and sand. This is happening everywhere, and it is not a coincidence. Perhaps it is related to the years of severe drought. (2) In various places, the crowing of roosters is heard at dusk. This is also happening everywhere, and everyone hears it together. According to historical records in our country, roosters crowing at unusual times is called "barren roosters" and is considered an ominous sound. The elders in Shaanxi folklore also have an old saying: "The rooster's crow early urges the delivery of grain and grass." At present, Shaanxi people speculate that the rooster's crow at dusk is actually a sign of military disaster. As for the situation in the various villages, it is desolate everywhere. Not a single tree can be seen, because they have all been felled by the troops or disaster victims for fuel. In the past, Zuo Zongtang, when he governed Gansu, ordered that green willows be planted from Tongguan along both sides of the main road, all the way to Lanzhou, for more than two thousand li. The soft branches and green canopy, the orioles singing at dawn, and the crows cawing in the evening were not only lovely scenery but also a blessing to travelers. A certain poet from Guanzhong once wrote a poem: "The road out of Xiaohan has ten thousand branches of willows, and travelers sing the Ode to the Great Wind." How lovely that was! But now, not only is not a single official willow tree left, but also not a single official or private tree in the various villages and towns has survived. It is truly a case of even the trees being in such a state, how can people bear it? But the authorities in Shaanxi turn a blind eye to it. Based on this, the problem of developing the Northwest is probably not easy to realize. (December 22nd)

Fujian's New Provincial Government Decides to Ban Opium and Gambling 55

And Has Already Strictly Banned Flower Gambling

Fuzhou Correspondence: Before the establishment of the new provincial government, it was widely rumored in Fuzhou and Xiamen that opium would be publicly sold and gambling dens would be opened to collect donations to alleviate financial difficulties. Therefore, after the establishment of the new provincial government, people in society paid great attention to these two matters. Opium addicts and gamblers were even more active, hoping to secure the franchise. A few days ago, Lei Shoupeng and Chen Zuguang, members of the Provincial Anti-Opium Association, specifically visited Fan Qiwu, the newly appointed Director of Finance, to inquire about the future anti-opium policy and request the allocation of funds owed to the association to facilitate its work. Fan replied that Chairman Chiang and Director Cai had recently discussed a plan to reorganize Fujian's finances and decided that, no matter how difficult it was, they would never seek military funds from within the scope of anti-opium measures and would absolutely adhere to the principle of complete prohibition. The association could continue to work hard according to this principle, and if there were difficulties or if military assistance was needed, he would do his best to help. He then allocated half a month's worth of funds to the association for its use. At the same time, the provincial government also issued a notice to the governments and public security bureaus of various counties in the provincial capital and northern Fujian, as well as to the commanders of the garrison troops, strictly prohibiting the prevalence of flower gambling, as it not only hindered the livelihood of ordinary people but also disrupted local security, and ordered the arrest of the ringleaders and punishment according to law. The notice stated: "Recently, reports from various sources indicate that flower gambling is prevalent in the villages surrounding the provincial capital and in various villages in northern Fujian, which is extremely detrimental to public morals. It is imperative to strictly investigate and prohibit it in order to curb the gambling trend and rectify public customs. Local administrative organs and garrison troops should assist in the investigation and prohibition, strictly arrest the ringleaders, and punish them according to law, and report back at any time." It is learned that in previous years, every winter, unscrupulous people in various villages would open flower gambling sessions in the mountains, inviting people to guess the results. Each session could collect thousands of yuan if there were many people, and hundreds of yuan if there were few people. The military and police agencies had regulations for collecting fees as protection. Villagers who lost their fortunes and committed suicide due to gambling were not uncommon. This trend is particularly prevalent this year. In the Fuzhu session in the southern countryside of the provincial capital alone, five or six thousand yuan could be collected every day, without interruption from autumn to winter. Everywhere in the city, there are "Ba Zai" [runners], with the foreign firms opened by Taiwanese people acting as the general collection agency. Every evening, groups of three or five people can be seen on the streets and alleys, inquiring about the results of the flower gambling or settling accounts for the wins and losses. After this strict prohibition, the gambling trend may be slightly curbed, and the rumors of opening gambling dens and selling opium may also be eliminated. (December 22nd)

Songjiang Creditors Meet 57

Regarding the bankruptcy of Songjiang Bank, after the county court pronounced its verdict on the 12th of this month, the creditors had many doubts. Yesterday (the 25th) at around 1:00 PM, they convened a creditors' meeting at the law office of Liu Zhimou. More than 70 people attended, including Zhuang Laotai and Shen Youren. Lawyer Qu Yue also attended the meeting. Zhang Zuoliu was elected chairman and Wu Boti was elected recorder. The matters resolved at the meeting were as follows: Regarding the county court's public notice of doubt, it was decided to: (A) Appeal according to law, (B) Petition the Ministry of Justice to investigate and correct the situation, (C) Send representatives to petition the Ministry of Justice. Regarding how to repay the appeal fees that have already been raised, it was decided that this fee will be shared proportionally by each creditor in the future. Regarding various procedural matters, it was decided to continue to request Lawyers Qu and Liu to act as agents.

Zhu Bingdie's Case Dismissed 59

Zhu Bingdie, the main writer for the local newspaper, was falsely accused of being a member of the Communist Party last month. ### Sun Ke Discusses Resisting Violence to Achieve Survival 66

A Shanghai Dispatch from the Shanghai Times News Agency: Yesterday, Sun Ke told reporters that he had not met with Chiang Kai-shek during his visit to Shanghai. He plans to go to Nanjing at the beginning of the New Year to assume his position as President of the Legislative Yuan. Reports that Japan intends to "settle accounts" with the Kuomintang because of the anti-Japanese resolutions passed by the Third Plenary Session are absurd. Although China is de facto conquered today, Japan's atrocities are evident to the world, surpassing even those of Germany before the European war. Universal justice has not disappeared, and there will surely be a day when the world delivers impartial judgment. At this critical moment of survival, we must strive for unity, act in concert as a nation, and resist violence together to achieve survival. If we rely solely on others without self-improvement, we will fall into decline, and who will be willing to support us? Subsequently, when the reporter inquired whether our country had made any military preparations in light of the urgent situation on the Rehe border, Sun replied that the military authorities must have made defensive arrangements. He hoped that the people would rise up to support them so that they could be implemented thoroughly, preventing violence from succeeding.

Hoping that All Military Personnel Will Voluntarily Enlist

Recently, taking advantage of our national officials' lack of resolve, and using our country's policy of distant friendship and close attack as a pretext, they have invaded the Rehe border. The survival of the nation is at stake; defending against aggression and saving the country, now is the time. Our associations swear with 120,000 sincere hearts to be your rear support. We are temporarily anxious and eagerly await news of victory. The various trade associations of Shanghai pay their respects, with seal.

Our troops, responsible for defending the country and guarding its territory, retreated without bloodshed, handing over a vast and beautiful land to the enemy. National sentiment was indignant and boiling over, and international observers were deeply shocked. Commemorating the Yunnan Uprising Yesterday 68

The Municipal Party Headquarters Convened a Meeting

Li Liejun Drank Bitterly and Composed Poetry

The Municipal Party Headquarters held a Yunnan Uprising Commemoration Meeting yesterday at 10:00 AM in the assembly hall on the third floor of the headquarters. Over 300 representatives from various organizations and party headquarters at all levels attended. Committee Member Long Tiyao chaired the meeting, with Zhang Hanyun acting as master of ceremonies. After the meeting was convened as usual, the chairman reported on the significance of the meeting. Subsequently, Committee Member Jiang Huaisu gave a speech on the recent situation of the Northeast Volunteer Army and how to provide effective relief. The original speech was quite long, so it is omitted. The meeting concluded with slogans at 12:00 PM.

The Two Road Party Headquarters held a Yunnan Uprising 17th Anniversary Commemoration Meeting yesterday in the assembly hall of the headquarters. Over 80 representatives from various organizations and all staff members signed in, totaling over 80 people. After the meeting was convened as usual, Chairman Wang Cheng reported on the historical facts of the Yunnan Uprising. This was followed by speeches by Tan Gengxin and Zhang Yunhe, whose words were passionate. The meeting then concluded with slogans.

The China Society: Yesterday, to commemorate the Yunnan Uprising, Li Liejun invited dozens of former colleagues from the Second National Protection Army to the China Society, where they discussed the past, full of impassioned songs and shedding many tears. Li stated at the meeting, "It has been sixteen years since Yunnan and Guizhou initiated the uprising against Yuan Shikai. Looking back now, I am deeply moved. Recalling the war against Yuan in the second year of the Republic, Yuan Shikai sent Li Chun, Cao Kun, and Ni Sichong to lead troops south, defeating the anti-Yuan army. After achieving their goals, they went their own way, thinking there was nothing to worry about. Those who worry about the country are always prepared for what is feared, but neglect what is not suspected. Yuan had no way to extend his influence over Yunnan and Guizhou, but the fact that Yunnan and Guizhou were able to initiate the uprising against Yuan had its reasons. Many of those who participated in and went through the uprising can speak about it, and the central government and various provinces have concise reports on the anniversary every year. Since the late Qing Dynasty, many members of the Tongmenghui who studied at military academies were distributed in Yunnan and Guangxi provinces, with Yunnan having even more. At that time, the completion of the Yunnan-Vietnam Railway and the emergency at Pianma caused panic among the people of Yunnan, who were already showing signs of revival. Members of the Tongmenghui served among them and proposed establishing a military academy, primary military school, and physical education school in the provincial capital to gather and educate talented individuals. The revolutionary spirit was thus spread throughout the province. When Li Zhongsheng was the governor of Guizhou and Yunnan, he worked hard on border affairs and was determined to train new troops. New and old talents were still able to be used together, and the foundation of the revolution was thus consolidated. At the same time, a small number of revolutionaries in Guizhou were also planning in secret, and Yunnan and Guizhou became a mutually supportive force. In the sixth year of the Republic, the provinces along the Yangtze River launched an uprising against Yuan. Because Yunnan and Guizhou were unable to participate, their strength was preserved. The financial and social situation was not destroyed, and all party members worked hard to govern the country, as if waiting for the time to arrive. When Yuan Shikai proclaimed himself emperor and sold out the country, the righteous indignation of Yunnan and Guizhou erupted. Those who directly led the matter at that time were Tang Genggeng, Liu Ruzhou, Cai Songpo, as well as Luo Rongxuan, Ren Kecheng, Li Yuegai, Zhou Huangfu, Dai Xunruo, Huang Feizhang, Fang Yunshong, Xiong Jinhan, and Cheng Songyun. Liejun also participated. Those who indirectly helped its success included Liang Rengong, Li Yinquan, Zhang Muxin, Du Yinqing, and Gong Zhenpeng. It cannot be said that all the talented people gathered, but the situation at that time was quite overwhelming. The value of the righteousness of Yunnan and Guizhou lies in its ability to pacify Sichuan in the north, stabilize Guangdong in the east, create a new situation in the southwest, and lay the foundation for the Northern Expedition in later years, completing the situation of the seventeenth year of the Republic. Its relationship is worthy of recording. However, past events are fleeting, and time flies. Recalling the friends who presided over military and political affairs, only Liejun, who is over fifty years old, is still lingering in the world. Foreign troubles are encroaching, and internal worries have not ended. Today's situation is truly beyond what was expected in those years. The first thing to do to save the crisis and seek survival is to unite and resist Japan. However, in order to unite and resist Japan, we must first seek national unity, and implementing national politics quickly is a clear path. Liejun and his friends have repeatedly suggested this to the central government and awakened the people for this reason. Although the National Political Council decided by the Third Plenary Session is almost comical, the National Assembly can still be expected to succeed, bringing it into the constitutional track. It is up to all comrades in the central government to sincerely plan for success, and the people of the whole country must rise up to form political organizations and go to it together." Afterwards, he recited a quatrain to show to the others present, with the poem: "Galloping in splendor, I recall the past, the drums of Yunnan and Guizhou reached the clouds. The sound of righteousness spread far and wide, moving You and Yan. How can we get Tang and Liu to defend the border again?" Zhong Bisheng then followed up with a poem: "How can there be the heroism of that year? Tang and Liu left, leaving it cold and desolate. The common people do not call for the Qin Emperor, but when the border horses are mute, they remember the phoenix feathers. Generously waving the whip, discussing the past, today, the Northeast is startled again. Can the Liaodong boar not lose to the Golden Horse? Why did Tang and Liu also defend the border?" Zhong was the Secretary-General of the Second National Protection Army in those years, and Li Heng described him as Chen Lin. The manifesto against Yuan in those years was written by Zhong, a famous scholar from Guangdong. The next one to follow was Yang Sugeng, with the poem: "The urgent messages are delayed for sixteen years, the troops moved from Yunnan to the Great Wall. In this seat, one drinks the Yellow Dragon, and it is given to the Jade Gate on the desolate border." The next one was Yu Dishan, who composed the poem: "The war has subsided for sixteen years, the Biji and Jinma are dim in the south. The walls of Yuantan are still unharmed, only the brave general is still guarding the border." The next one was Tao Xingru, who composed the poem: "Counting the years, it has been sixteen years, the righteous indignation of that time reached the clouds. If Tang and Liu were still here today, how could they bear to see the eastern neighbors cut off our borders?" The next one was Wu Zhaoxuan, who composed the poem: "Following the whip and stirrup for twenty years, one pillar in the southeast is enough to support the sky. Now the national crisis is even more dangerous, I wish to rise up in the east and defend the border in history." The whole room was filled with a lively atmosphere, and everyone raised their glasses and drank together, no less than the heroism of those years. The gathering only dispersed joyfully at 3:00 PM in the afternoon.

Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bonds Begin to be Claimed Today 69

Public Bond Tickets Were Sent to Shanghai by the Ministry of Finance the Night Before

The Foundation Entrusted the National Products Bank to Handle It

The governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, in order to rescue the silk factories in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, specially requested the Ministry of Finance to issue 3 million yuan in public bonds. Any silk factory that had stockpiled silk or silkworm cocoons, and had been registered and qualified by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Stockpiled Silk and Silkworm Cocoon Committee, would be given a subsidy of 100 taels per dan when exporting, equivalent to 140 yuan in public bonds. The joint office of the Stockpiled Silk Sales Committee and the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Stockpiled Silk and Silkworm Cocoon Committee began operating on the 16th of this month. The public bond tickets were also brought to Shanghai by a special commissioner sent by the Ministry of Finance the night before, and were temporarily kept by the Public Bond Verification Committee of the Ministry of Finance. The governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces had previously telegraphed the Ministry of Finance, requesting that the silk industry public bonds be issued by the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Public Bond Foundation Committee. Yesterday, Zheng Lai, the Director of the Public Bond Department of the Ministry, received a telegram from the Ministry notifying the Foundation Custody Committee, and the Chairman of the Committee, Tai Runqing, and the Standing Committee Member, Ye Zhuotang, claimed the bonds and entrusted the National Products Bank on Third Avenue in the city to issue them on their behalf. Any silk merchants who have already exported stockpiled silk can exchange the subsidy certificate from the Organizing Committee for public bond tickets from today.

Notifying the Provision of Support to the 11th Route Army 74

Now, the Overseas Chinese United Association has sent a letter inquiring about the situation. A letter was sent to the association yesterday stating: "In reply, your letter of November 17th, introducing Liu Zhenbang and others, representatives of the 11th Route Army of the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army, to the Association to report on the combat situation of the route. Subsequently, the representatives sincerely requested assistance with cotton clothing and ammunition. While under verification, another letter was received on November 26th, again urging assistance to the troops. We immediately donated winter clothing that had been collected nearby in succession and allocated it first, totaling 1,604 items of cotton quilts, blankets, cotton clothing, and military uniforms. The representatives of the route, Liu Zhenbang and Zhan Guoshu, issued receipts for the items. Additionally, we requested Mr. Zhang Peinian to allocate 800 yuan for travel expenses, which was also received. We have heard that your association has sent personnel to investigate, and you should be able to understand the actual situation. Although the amount of assistance provided by our association this time is small, we hope that the troops can take actual action, so as not to fail the expectations of the people. We hereby inform you of this and hope that you will inform the headquarters of the route. This is addressed to the Overseas Chinese United Association." The association also replied to inquiries from Wu Zonglian, Cai Yuanpei, Li Liejun, and others, stating: "In reply, we have received your letter of November 28th, and we understand everything. Representatives Liu Zhenbang and Zhan Guoshu from Dong Rongji's troops of the 11th Route Army of the Northeast People's Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army were introduced to the Association by the Overseas Chinese United Association to report on the situation and request assistance for the troops. Subsequently, it was decided to allocate a total of 1,604 items of cotton quilts, blankets, cotton clothing, and military uniforms, and 800 yuan for travel expenses, which were all separately claimed by Liu Zhan. We hope that you will inform Mr. Cai Yuanpei and other gentlemen.

The Postal Savings Bureau to Be Merged; Zhu Jiahua's Letter to Wu Tiecheng 75

Name Changed and Subordinated to the Postal Administration

Senior Staff to Be Selected from Specialized Talents

Strict Screening and Examination System to Be Implemented

A reporter from the Shen Shi Telegraph Agency visited Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua yesterday and inquired about the merger of the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau. Mr. Zhu kindly showed a recent letter to Mayor Wu of this city. The details are disclosed as follows:

Respectfully, Mr. Tiecheng: Previously, the Postal Economic System Research Committee delegated representatives to submit a draft plan for the merger of the Specialized Savings and Remittance Bureau and sought the Ministry's opinion. At that time, due to the beginning of my term and the Ministry of Education not yet handed over, matters were complicated. Moreover, this case is of great importance, and a response could not be given hastily without thorough consideration. Subsequently, after reviewing old files and studying the draft plan along with various opinions and other reference materials, I deeply felt that the key to consolidating the postal foundation lies not in the separation or combination of postal services and savings and remittance but in the need for improvement in both businesses themselves. In the past two years, following the Northeast Incident and the Shanghai War, the national public and private economies have suffered the same difficulties. As a result, the postal service has been hit hard, and the savings and remittance business, which relies on the transfer of its surplus for support, has also been affected. Now, in terms of the improvement that should be sought in the savings and remittance business, what we should pay urgent attention to is how to ensure the safety of savings and make good use of them to seek the interests of depositors, and how to develop the savings and remittance business in order to achieve financial circulation and increase the people's savings strength. This is a fundamental plan. The development of the savings and remittance business can help the postal foundation to be consolidated with its assistance, and the benefits to the country and the people will be even greater. Therefore, in order to enable the savings and remittance business to achieve this mission, two important principles should be implemented in its system: strict supervision and professional development. Since the separation and specialized operation of the savings and remittance business, savings have increased from more than 11 million yuan to more than 27 million yuan, and remittances have increased from more than 13.33 million yuan to more than 16.11 million yuan. It seems that this cannot be said to be the result of moving towards professional development. However, upon examining the actual situation, the scope of savings investment is not strict, and it is almost competing with ordinary commercial banks. This may be the source of criticism. Moreover, since savings are the accumulation of the people's scattered hard-earned money, ensuring safety is the primary task. The current method has not yet been implemented to the best possible level, which is undeniable. However, looking back to the past when they were combined, what was the situation regarding these two important principles? In the past, when post offices handled savings and remittance business, all systems and methods followed everything of the postal service. There were no strict supervision regulations, and those in charge often did not understand financial matters. Most of their savings investments were deposited in foreign banks, purchased foreign stocks and foreign bonds. This was not a comprehensive consideration for the interests of the country and the people. The so-called strict supervision means that accounting must be independent, auditing must be thorough, and examining the scope and nature of capital utilization and whether the collateral is safe and profitable are all extremely important points. The so-called professional development means that savings and remittance business is different from postal business. Savings and remittance belong to the financial nature and are not like postal business, which only requires handling internal work, being quick in handling affairs, and meticulous in procedures. More attention must be paid to the situation in the economic and financial circles. Therefore, the personnel in charge must have financial knowledge and experience, and the management methods must also adapt to the environment and actual conditions of the market. How can it be appropriate to order the post office to handle it completely in a mixed manner? Therefore, in order to consolidate the postal foundation, we should also strive to improve the operation of the savings and remittance business, so that its system has the characteristics of strict supervision and professional development. The reasons and necessity are very obvious. Some commentators often say that in the early years, savings and remittances were not very developed, and it seemed too early to separate and specialize them. This statement is not without merit. However, now that it has been specialized for two years, the scale has been established, and the business has gradually developed. Even if we examine its expenses, it is not as huge as the criticisms claim. If it is suddenly cancelled and restored to the old system, it is inevitable that it will cause too much disturbance and affect the credit of savings and remittances. Moreover, even this is not a truly fundamental consideration. Therefore, the current plan is to urgently improve its system, correct the inadequacies of the past, and establish a permanent and good foundation. On the one hand, a strict supervision system is used to ensure that the interests of the people are truly emphasized and the safety of depositors is protected. On the other hand, its professional development is maintained to make its content sound. At the same time, we should also strive to increase the spirit of cooperation between savings and remittance and postal services in order to achieve mutually beneficial results. After several studies, based on the above principles and spirit, it is planned to change the name of the Postal Savings and Remittance General Bureau to the Postal Savings Bureau and subordinate it to the Postal Department, so that it can be connected and cooperate with the postal business. In terms of personnel and administration, strict laws and regulations will be formulated to establish a good system. Senior staff will be carefully selected from those who have knowledge and experience in the financial business, so that they are all specialized talents in order to achieve the goal of professional development. As for the rest of the middle and lower-level staff, in addition to screening the current staff, an examination system should be adopted in the future. Laws and regulations should also be established for those engaged in postal work to have the opportunity to participate in the examination. The treatment should be guaranteed so that they can work with peace of mind and improve work efficiency. In terms of expenditure, efforts should be made to economize, and those that should be cut should be cut in order to ensure that people are not used in vain and money is not wasted in vain. As for the accounting aspect, at the beginning of the establishment of savings, the accounting was originally independent, and there was a savings name. However, the director of the bureau was concurrently the director of the Postal General Bureau. After the separation, the savings and remittance income was transferred to the Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, while in terms of expenditure, all post offices that concurrently handle savings and remittance business had all expenses incurred due to savings and remittance business listed as postal expenses. This is not very consistent with the principle of independent accounting. In the future, the Postal Savings Bureau will be subordinate to the Postal Bureau, and all income and expenditure accounts of savings and remittance business should be set up separately, except that the surplus should be included in the postal accounting general report, so that it is not mixed with postal income and expenditure. The expenses incurred by post offices that concurrently handle savings and remittance business due to savings and remittance should also be verified and borne by the Savings and Remittance Bureau as appropriate. In addition, for the method of strict supervision, it is planned to establish a Postal Savings Supervision Committee. In addition to representatives from the public opinion organs and the Control Yuan, the Accounting Department, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Transportation, and the Postal General Bureau, the Ministry of Transportation will also select representatives with outstanding qualifications from several important industrial, commercial, and financial groups. The Ministry will select several people to jointly form a committee to implement effective supervision. The committee will also appoint accountants at any time to review the accounts and publish reports in order to make them public, so as to ensure the safety of savings and make the savings and remittance business sound. In addition, detailed laws and regulations will be strictly formulated to strictly limit the scope and types of savings investment and its amount in order to prevent unexpected risks. All of these are intended to emphasize the principles of strict supervision and professional development, and to achieve the intention of consolidating the postal foundation and increasing the spirit of cooperation in improving the savings and remittance business itself in order to achieve mutually beneficial results. Originally, the postal service and remittance business are both national transportation businesses. The surplus of savings and remittance belongs to the surplus of transportation, and the deficit of the postal service belongs to the deficit of transportation. It is reasonable to use this to support that. Looking at past examples, it is even more evident that if the credit of savings is affected by the dispute over separation and combination of related businesses belonging to the same entity, how can this be the original intention of protecting the postal service and savings and remittance? In short, various businesses have been in a state of decline in recent years, partly due to the dangerous environment and partly due to their own unsoundness. There is nothing that does not need to be reorganized and improved. There is no way to improve that does not require us to sacrifice the spirit of public service beyond the system. My humble opinions on seeking the root of the matter and discussing the matter are honored to be inquired, and I dare to report them. I hope that the committee members of your esteemed society will give me their advice. I wish you all the best. Sincerely, Zhu Jiahua. December 22, 21st year of the Republic.

Striking Messengers of Great Northern and Other Companies Petitioned the Taxpayers' Association and Chinese Directors 81

Requesting Assistance, Which Was Granted, and Undertaking Mediation

The Labor Union Issued a Declaration Explaining the Process

The Xin Sheng News Agency reported that after the messengers of the Great Northern, Great Eastern, and Pacific Telegraph Companies went on strike, the situation became deadlocked. The workers delegated representatives to petition the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Concession and the Chinese directors of the Municipal Council and issued a declaration. The details are as follows:

Petitioning the Taxpayers' Association: The striking workers, seeing that the company's attitude was tough and the mediation of the party and government agencies was ineffective, had no choice but to delegate representatives to petition the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the Public Concession, requesting assistance. They then went to the Municipal Council and requested assistance from Chinese directors Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Ludeng, and others to avoid unemployment. They were all received and agreed to undertake mediation in order to resolve the situation as soon as possible and avoid affecting social order. As for the company, since it hired Western children to take over the delivery work, it has often been delayed due to unfamiliarity with Chinese characters. For example, Dongjuchang Neiyutai Dongshenzhuang on Sichuan Road and Tongrenchang in the South City have all sent letters to the company criticizing the delays caused by Western children's delivery.

Labor Union's Declaration Seeking Assistance: The Shanghai Third District Foreign Merchants' Telegraph Delivery Industry Workers' Union issued a special declaration yesterday seeking assistance, stating, "Our workers serve in the Great Northern, Great Eastern, and Pacific companies. We work hard and dare not slack off. For example, during the January 28th Incident this year, we often went into the dangerous war zone amidst gunfire and within the defense lines of the dwarves. Because there were places where the language was not understood, there were also those who were injured by the Japanese soldiers' gun butts, but there was nowhere to complain, so we had to endure it in our hearts. All telegrams were delivered as usual without any obstruction, so that the company's business could develop. However, the capitalists did not give any rewards, but instead despised our workers and did not think about the dangerous and laborious achievements. They used cunning methods to oppress the workers. If the workers made any mistakes, they would be fired immediately. For example, in November this year, the number eight messenger of the Great Northern Company was occasionally ill. The company did not allow him to take leave. He personally delivered telegrams to nearby places, but it was difficult to support the faraway ones. He entrusted the Great Eastern Company to deliver a telegram on his behalf and mistook the door number ten, which happened to be the residence of the Great Northern Company's manager. He was immediately reprimanded. After sending it accurately and returning to the company, the manager reported it to the general manager, who immediately fired the number eight messenger. The workers believed that the mistake of mistaking the door number was very minor. Why should he be fired? The workers begged the general manager twice to reinstate him. If there were other mistakes in the future, he could be fired, but the capitalists insisted on the imperialist policy and resolutely refused. Thinking about this situation, the capitalists are completely using oppressive methods to treat the workers. In recent years, postal services, customs, and railways are all transportation agencies. The wages and benefits enjoyed by the workers are generous and can barely provide food and clothing, while the telegraph is also one of the transportation agencies, but its wages are comparatively very different, and it is difficult to maintain a livelihood. The workers consulted each other and made nine requests to the capitalists on November 25, but the company first accepted and then reneged, and then perfunctorily. The workers urged repeatedly, but there was no sincere response. Our workers could not bear it and were forced to go on strike on the 20th of this month, hoping that the company would realize it. However, the capitalists still used tough methods to treat the workers, intending to destroy them and wanting to put all the members of our union in a desperate situation. Representatives were sent to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau to mediate, but it was ineffective. The capitalists are really said to be ignorant of human feelings. Our workers are suffering from this environmental oppression under the clear blue sky and bright sun. It is very painful! We beg the labor unions of all circles to give public assistance so that the workers of our union can have a glimmer of glory and the labor unrest can be resolved. Then all the workers of our union will be infinitely grateful! A declaration by all the workers."

The Rice Industry Association of this city received a letter from the county government yesterday, which stated, "Regarding the excessively low price of rice, which is harmful to people's livelihood, we urgently need to provide relief. We intend to request your association to advocate, in addition to benefiting merchants, to donate funds for grain reserves in this county on an annual basis to benefit people's livelihood. This is not a small matter. We should communicate this to you, hoping that you will investigate and consider the matter and reply. We are deeply grateful."

Record of the Standing Committee Meeting of the Jiangsu Rice Federation 83

The Jiangsu Ninghu City and County Rice Industry Association Federation held the fourteenth meeting of the second session of the executive and supervisory committees at Cuixiu Hall at 3 pm yesterday. The members present were Li Zhongchen, Qian Jingsheng, Lu Zhuqing, Zhao Zixin (representing Ren Xunxian), Gong Zhaoming, Chen Junyu, Yan Xiaoquan, Zhu Zhaoxi, Zhu Zixiang, and others, totaling nine people. Zhu Zixiang was publicly elected as chairman. After performing the rituals, the chairman reported that the previous telegram requesting the provincial government to quickly circulate rice to alleviate the suffering of farmers in Jiangsu has now received approval from the provincial government No. 2337, stating, "We have received your telegram. After investigation, the provincial government's 551st committee meeting decided to allow the temporary sale of rice and wheat out of the province. However, it must be submitted by the county government and transferred to this government for the issuance of a passport for investigation. Passports will not be charged. If they are transported out of the province without a passport, they will still be punished according to the regulations. Please be informed." Following this, there was a discussion on the case of whether the rice industry peers in Shanghai City should implement a new system of measuring instruments starting next year and whether peers in the interior should consult in advance. It was decided to hold the next standing committee meeting early for discussion.

The Overseas Chinese Federation Welcomed Returning Overseas Chinese 84

A 72-Year-Old Man Is Willing to Fight the Japanese

The Overseas Chinese Federation held three special committee meetings at 2 pm yesterday to separately deliberate on the new charter, the establishment methods of the Overseas Chinese Club, and various preparations related to the election of new directors. At 4 pm, a tea party was held in the hall of the association to welcome returning overseas Chinese Zhang Wenbing, Chen Bingsan, Ding Hongnan, and Xu Youfan. Zhang Wenbing is a major mine owner from Selangor, British Malaya. Chen Bingsan is the former secretary-general of the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Group in Luzon. Ding Hongnan is the principal of the Sentaro Chinese School in the Philippines. Xu Youfan is the president of the Burmese Chinese General Chamber of Commerce. First, Chairman Xu (Jigong) and Secretary-General Huang (Jianzhong) gave welcoming speeches and reported on the association's affairs. Then, Zhang Wenbing talked about his work upon returning to China, saying that he is an overseas Chinese from Guangdong and a 72-year-old man who operates tin mines in Malaya with more than 20,000 workers. Currently, due to the very bad economic situation, the workers will lose their jobs. He returned to China to discuss with the government to move these 20,000 workers to the three northeastern provinces to reclaim wasteland. Before he arrived in China, the three northeastern provinces had already fallen into the hands of the enemy, so he discussed with the Nanjing government to choose a location near the three northeastern provinces to reclaim wasteland and arm themselves against Japan. The government expressed its approval. After returning to Shanghai, he inspected Songhu, where there was war everywhere, leaving not a tree or a blade of grass, which was really heartbreaking. He said this with tears in his voice, and the audience was moved. Zhang then said that there are tens of thousands of young people and veterans in Guangdong who are willing to go to the customs to kill the enemy, but they have no travel expenses and there is nothing they can do. The rich people of our country should have considerable feelings. After he returns to Malaya, he will find a way to send this batch of workers back to China. This old man is also willing to go to the customs with the strong men to kill the enemy. With only a few years left in his old age, it is time to risk his life at this time. Even if he dies, he is willing to die under the guns of the dwarfs. Then, Chen Bingsan reported that there are more than 100 national salvation groups in the Philippines, with 130,000 overseas Chinese. The workers donated very enthusiastically to the volunteer army, borrowing money and saving household expenses to donate voluntarily. In less than ten days, they reached more than 50,000 yuan. In three weeks, they donated tens of thousands of yuan for air defense. There are many overseas Chinese who love the country, but there are also many shameless traitors who are rich and powerful and live comfortably. The young people are angry at their shamelessness, so they secretly formed assassination groups and bloodbath groups to eliminate these scums. In legal terms, many lawsuits are lost for detaining Japanese goods, so they adopted other boycott methods. Chinese businessmen in various places successively sued traitors in batches, making the traitors exhausted. This method is quite effective. We should thank the Philippine customs and the Filipinos. They have helped us a lot in our work to resist Japanese goods. Xu Youfan and Ding Hongnan also reported the overseas Chinese situation in various places in detail, which is omitted. More than 50 people attended the meeting that day and dispersed happily at 6 pm.

Donations Received by the Support Association for Righteous Armies of Liaoning, Jilin, Heilongjiang, and Jehol 86

Fundraising by Night School for Industrial Workers to Aid

Colonel Hawke of the U.S. Passes Away Suddenly in Zhejiang 87

Chinese and Foreign Friends Express Regret

Colonel Hawke, commander of the Fourth Regiment of the U.S. Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai, went out to buy Christmas items the morning before yesterday (the 23rd). He was in good spirits and showed no signs of illness. He returned to his residence at 927 Avenue Joffre before noon for lunch, then began wrapping gifts for children. Suddenly, his heart failed, and he died instantly. Colonel Hawke was born in California, USA, in 1877. He served in the Marine Corps for 32 years. In October 1930, he was promoted to commander of the Fourth Regiment of the U.S. Marine Corps stationed in Shanghai. He was respected by his subordinates and was particularly devoted to public welfare. He had a wide circle of friends. Therefore, when the news of his death spread, Chinese and foreign friends expressed their regret. The date of the funeral has not yet been determined, as it is necessary to await instructions from Washington.

Measures to Save on Telegraph Fees 88

Shanghai Telegraph Bureau to Implement on New Year's Day

Telephone Numbers to Replace Names and Addresses

In order to improve the speed and reduce the cost of sending telegrams in various places, the Ministry of Communications had previously drafted a plan to use the recipient's installed telephone number as their name and address, thereby reducing the number of characters and saving on telegraph fees. It is now learned that this measure has been approved by Minister Zhu Jiahua and has been circulated to telecommunications agencies under his jurisdiction to implement it in accordance with local conditions. It is reported that the International Radio Station of the Ministry of Communications in this city, the Shanghai Radio General Station, and the Shanghai Telegraph Bureau have decided to implement it starting on New Year's Day next year. However, if the recipient has not installed a telephone, the procedure will remain the same to ensure delivery.

A Criminal Escapes from the Train While Being Escorted to Suzhou for Appeal 93

A Bailiff Jumps Down to Chase

But Sprains His Ankle

Hu Zhaoyu, a native of Wuxi, was detained by the Shanghai Local Court for a rape case in Shanghai. Because he appealed, the court dispatched bailiff Wang Benchu on the 24th of this month (the day before yesterday) to escort the criminal on the 7:30 a.m. fourth-class train to Suzhou. When the train traveled about five or six li from Nanxiang Station, the criminal suddenly wanted to defecate. The bailiff escorted him to the toilet and monitored him. However, the toilet of the fourth-class train was equipped like an ordinary train station toilet, so its height was parallel to the window. Unexpectedly, the criminal intended to escape and took the opportunity to jump out of the window. Because his body was agile, as if he had been trained in sports or martial arts, he ran away as soon as he jumped down. The bailiff saw this and immediately leaned over to grab him, but it was too late. The bailiff immediately handed over four large packages of files, three official letters, and his own hat to the ticket inspector for safekeeping, and then immediately jumped down, resulting in a sprained ankle. However, he was already four or five li away from the place of escape. The bailiff immediately chased after him with all his might, but has not yet caught him. All files and official letters have been handed over by the Nanxiang Station staff to the First Section Railway Police Department for safekeeping. Yesterday, the Police Department telephoned the court to report the situation and requested that personnel be sent to retrieve the files.

The Method of Striking a Foot Stove Cover to Find a Lost Child Proves Effective 94

Deng Baozi Hears His Father's Shout

And Comes Out of the Room in Response

Four Kidnappers Were Arrested

And Another Girl Was Rescued

Deng Baozi, the six-year-old son of Guo Hongming, a vegetable vendor from Jiangbei who lives at No. 12 Xixiang Lane, Lafayette Road, in the French Concession, was abducted by bandits at the Tangjiawan vegetable market on the 12th of this month and hidden in the home of a Yangzhou woman, Shi Jiang, on the upper floor of No. 30, Orre Road. That afternoon, Guo struck a foot stove cover to search for him and shouted the child's name along Orre Road. Deng Baozi heard the sound and escaped. Father and son met, and after inquiring about what had happened, they reported it to the police station. The police sent detectives to arrest kidnapper Shi Jiang, Shi Chen, and suspected accomplices Tian Qigui and Jiang Yin, and also rescued another abducted six-year-old girl, Chen Amao. The detectives investigated and confirmed that the girl was Chen Ai Jin, the daughter of Mr. Chen of Pike Road, and that she had been renamed after being abducted. They issued a notice for her to be claimed. The kidnappers were escorted to the Second Special District Court, where the police lawyer filed a public prosecution in accordance with the law. After the interrogation was completed, Shi Jiang and Shi Chen were ordered to await sentencing. Tian Qigui and Jiang Yin were released on the grounds of no involvement in the case. On the day of sentencing the day before yesterday, Judge Li Changnian presided over the case and sentenced Shi Jiang to three years and six months of imprisonment for the crime of hiding men and women under the age of twenty who were abducted for profit, and Shi Chen (for the same crime) to two years and six months of imprisonment as a warning.

Minutes of the Joint Meeting of the Zhabei Disaster-Stricken Households 96

The Zhabei Disaster-Stricken Households Joint Association held its tenth representative meeting yesterday afternoon at 2:00 p.m. More than twenty people attended, including He Yongjia, He Huijun, Yu Wenjiang, Shen Wenbin, Xi Xiaomao, and Xi Ronglin.
