Economy Special

The Way Out of the Current Economic Panic: The Relationship Between Recession and a Poor Monetary System 151

— Written by Gustav Cassel of Sweden, Translated by Xie Juceng

The following article was recently written by the famous Swedish economist Cassel, and it contains keen insights into the main causes of the current global recession and the ways to alleviate it in the future. It will be considered at the upcoming World Economic Conference. It is specially translated and published below.

We live in the richest world that has ever existed, but there are still millions of people on the verge of starvation. At the same time, a portion of the world's population is exposed to terrible poverty, and the situation is getting worse day by day. At least twenty million good workers have no jobs to find, and the number of those who can only find half-day jobs is increasing daily. Many private shops and entire trades are collapsing one after another, and more and more countries are unable to pay their debts.

Since defaulting and the inability to repay debts are so widespread, people have begun to abandon natural facts, and there is no longer any respect for obligations. If things continue like this, it will truly be a great danger to the entire social order, with no end in sight. Why can't humanity make full use of the great resources at its disposal? Why can't we increase production so that prosperity increases year by year, so that everyone can enjoy this prosperity?

One of the most common answers to this question is that progress was too fast in the eight or nine years after 1920, so the result was inevitably a reversal. But do not believe these words.

Many people believe that production rates must be reduced in the future to give consumers time to absorb, so that supply and demand can be balanced. This is completely meaningless. Consumption is determined by production itself. The result of production should never lead to an excessively narrow absorption.

Furthermore, statistics can prove that the development of production between 1922 and 1929 did not increase unusually in general. The economic life at that time only recovered to the rate of progress before the war. There is no reason why such progress should not continue.

Therefore, the assertion that the climax of the speculative craze in 1929 was an important reason for the subsequent economic decline is also generally untenable. Of course, in the United States, the soaring stock prices in the stock exchange were the main reason for the subsequent sharp drop in stock prices. But to say that this kind of regulation of the stock exchange caused a major disruption to the machinery of production and consumption is simply nonsense.

So, why did this healthy development encounter such unfortunate setbacks halfway? There is no other answer than to say that the world's monetary structure collapsed, and there is no need for any other answer. This is simply the result of extremely poor management of the monetary structure. In the early years after 1920, when most countries in the world returned to the gold standard, the author had already said in 1920 that because there was not much gold supply, only the major countries could cooperate on a deliberate gold-saving policy. For the monetary need for gold, there should be a systematic restriction, so that the gold standard would have sufficient stability. This policy naturally included a reasonable distribution of gold between foreign countries. If a few countries want to drag a lot of gold into their own pockets, it should be restrained. If everyone could truly implement this gold-saving policy at a certain time, then the world could enjoy great progress and prosperity.

However, this balance continued to be threatened by a serious situation, which was the payment of reparations and the burden of war debts. These payments clearly exceeded the world's ordinary payment function. If this machine cannot be adjusted, and war debts cannot be made payable, then the last resort is for the debtor countries to be forced to export gold, and for the creditor countries to receive this gold to offset the payments.

Among them, the United States and France were the most prominent. If they lowered their tariff rates, on the one hand, and expressed their best efforts to facilitate the repayment of debts by debtor countries, whether by goods or services, it would be acceptable. In this way, the special difficulty of this payment transfer could be avoided. But the opposite was true. Both countries increased their tariff rates and exhausted every effort to restrict this method of repayment, because they feared that their domestic markets would be subjected to foreign competition.

However, even with this tariff protection policy, the adjustment of the payment balance was temporarily possible, because the receiving countries were willing to extend huge amounts of credit to the world. For example, France mostly accumulated short-term balances overseas, and the United States supplied the world with huge amounts of capital for many years. Therefore, the international payment balance was still maintained very smoothly.

However, this system did not have true stability. As soon as those countries expressed their unwillingness to export capital, the system would collapse immediately. This can be exemplified by France. When France restored the gold standard in the middle of 1928, she began to accumulate large amounts of gold, partly helped by her previously held overseas balances. As a result, capital exports turned into imports. Furthermore, in the United States, domestic demand for capital increased daily, and since the stock market turmoil in 1929, the United States' ability to export capital was naturally greatly affected. At the same time, Germany in Europe had also exhausted her borrowing capacity.

Under these circumstances, the continued repayment of war debts only resulted in France and the United States accumulating large amounts of gold, and as a result, the gold reserves of other countries in the world were greatly reduced. These reserves usually increased by about 3% each year, but as a result of the above changes, there was a shortage of 2-3% by 1931. As for the reduction of the gold reserve ratio beyond the legal limit, it goes without saying. As a result, the competition of prices in the world market was subjected to a severe pressure, and world prices showed an unprecedented disastrous fall.

It needs to be explained here why the accumulation of large amounts of gold by France and the United States never produced some repayment function to raise the domestic prices of the receiving countries. According to the classical theory of the automatic operation of the gold standard, such price increases are the result of the influx of gold, and once this effect occurs, it can curb the influx of gold, and finally become a reversal of the situation.

However, France and the United States tried to avoid using the new gold they obtained for this purpose. Most of the gold was only stored in the vaults of the central banks, and as a result of the credit restriction policy, not only could these domestic prices not be increased, but they even fell sharply, regardless of the continued influx of gold.

In summary, the repayment of war debts, along with the unwillingness to accept ordinary goods in exchange, caused an unreasonable demand for the world's monetary gold reserves. Moreover, the plaintiffs did not make proper use of the accumulated gold. How could the world prices not plummet?

Many countries that lost gold were forced to abandon the gold standard when they ran out of resources. They felt that domestic prices and wages could not be reduced, especially the burden of their public and private debts. Therefore, they felt that it was impossible to reduce the international price equalization. They had no other way to change except to abandon the gold standard in order to sever the relationship between domestic prices and the price of gold. As a result, the entire gold standard system in the world was completely on the verge of collapse.

Under this environment, the first thing to do is obviously to find a way to remove the ultimate results lurking behind these unfortunate developments that we are currently facing. For this reason, there are calls for the cancellation of reparations and war debts. However, we should understand the true meaning of this cancellation movement.

Now, almost twelve years of experience have proven that the payment of war debts and reparations has led the world's monetary mechanism to destruction. The current panic is enough to prove that the world's economic life can no longer tolerate such a situation. Therefore, the world is extremely concerned about the removal of these political payments. This seems like a great sacrifice, but compared with the various disasters caused by the current panic, it is simply a drop in the bucket.

The annual war debt payments received by the United States are actually less than 1% of the losses suffered by the American people due to the current recession. Therefore, canceling war debts is a good way to prosper commerce, and the whole world can hope for recovery as a result.

There is no doubt that the previous payments of war debts have caused such destruction to the world, so it is not enough to simply cancel war debts in the future. We must also use active measures to restore prosperity. Among them, the most important and urgent need is to raise prices, because those prices have no natural need to fall at all. Only the poor management of the world's monetary system has artificially made the relationship between wholesale prices, retail prices, cost of living, wages, and debt interest rates uneven. To make this imbalance balanced, there is only one way: to raise wholesale prices.

People are confused by past lessons, so when they hear about raising prices, they try their best to oppose it. You should know that under normal circumstances, inflation is indeed not a very good thing. But if we have just come out of a forced contraction, then it is necessary to adopt a considerable method of inflation to cure the diseases caused by contraction.

However, this kind of inflation plan, at the beginning, must be placed under the control of the authorities, and the public must understand an accurate inflation procedure. The purpose should be to raise prices and make them close to the price standard of 1928 as the accurate criterion.

If this plan is recognized as the official policy of the country, it will be easy to achieve results. People can understand that this is not an uncontrolled or unlimited inflation, and they do not need to worry about the future of their currency. On the other hand, they believe that the rise in prices will naturally lead producers to work harder on production. As for what this relies on the authorities, it is only necessary to set a clear goal and adopt a clear policy and strive to achieve it.

Naturally, this plan can increase much credibility if the world's major trading countries, such as the United Kingdom and the United States, can cooperate hand in hand. If they can reach an understanding on a common policy to raise the prices of their own currencies, they will have the ability to influence the world. Other countries will naturally scramble to join this policy.

This move, of course, does not need to be delayed until after the International Economic Conference is convened. If these two leading countries first start working on the first step of raising prices, it will undoubtedly make the progress of this conference easier.

As for the restoration of the gold standard, that is out of the question. It is too early to try to do this now, and it is also questionable whether the international monetary system can be restored to the gold standard. It is certainly impossible before certain important conditions are fulfilled.

The cancellation of war debts is the first step of these conditions, and the second step is to agree on an organized gold-saving policy, including reducing the customary needs of central banks in various countries for gold reserves. The third condition is to restore considerable freedom of international trade and international capital movement. You can never have any stable international monetary system if it is not based on a connected, reliable, and stable international economic system.

Anyone who pays close attention to these conditions can immediately realize that if the issue of restoring the international gold standard system is raised before the Economic Conference, it will not only be useless, but it will also be unsightly. The only result will be endless discussions that will eventually lead to nothing.

International economic cooperation, such as restoring the freedom and stability of international movement of goods and capital, as it was before the European War, is really indispensable and cannot be delayed. The entire system of restricting foreign exchange transactions and import quantities must first be abolished, followed by lowering tariff rates, and then the international exchange of goods can be expanded as much as possible. This is really a necessary condition for the prosperity of the world.

In our opinion, this restoration work must be carried out in three aspects simultaneously. War debts must be canceled, prices must be raised, and some kind of trade freedom must be restored. It is useless to wait and see each other or implement them one after another. We must do it immediately. We cannot wait any longer, otherwise not only will our economic bankruptcy be imminent, but Western civilization will also end with it. Fortunately, the Lausanne Conference has done a good job in removing the main obstacles that stand in the way of recovery. This is exactly the time to start active work.

Recent Overview of Salt Affairs in Guangdong Province 152

The establishment of national salt affairs audit agencies originated from loan contracts. Upon the establishment of the Five-Nation Consortium Loan in the second year of the Republic (1913), our nation's salt administration became subject to foreign supervision. Twenty years have passed since then. The salt base of our country is Nanjing. Former Finance Minister Gu Yingfen once merged the salt affairs audit agencies into the local salt transport commissioner's offices. This was a unification of the audit and administrative departments from a state of separation. However, not long after the proposal was made, Song Ziwen succeeded him and restored the previously merged audit agencies, thus separating them again. Guangdong is one such example. Here is a brief account of the recent situation of salt affairs in Guangdong Province:

Guangdong Province, located in the southern part of the country, has maintained its original state due to special political circumstances. It has not been convenient to make changes. Therefore, although there has been a recent proposal for audit chiefs to concurrently hold administrative positions, as in Liangzhe, Lianghuai, Shandong, and the four areas along the Yangtze River, Guangdong Province still follows the old rules, with administration and auditing remaining independent. The salt affairs administrative agencies in Guangdong Province are the Liangguang Salt Transport Commissioner's Office, along with various deputy transport commissioner's offices and tax and transport bureaus, and salt police teams, all under its jurisdiction. The audit agency is the Guangdong Salt Affairs Audit Sub-office, with audit branch offices in Chaoqiao and Pingnan Gui in Shantou and Beihai, and three tax bureaus in Huizhou, Yangjiang, and Shanwei, namely Dongjiang, Enchun, and Hailufeng. In total, there are about seventy bureaus and checkpoints of various sizes in the entire region, collecting tens of millions in taxes annually.

Guangdong salt is sold in Guangdong, Guangxi, Fujian, Guizhou, Jiangxi, and Yunnan provinces. In Guangdong, it is sold in eighty counties, including Nanhai, etc. In Guangxi, it is sold in seventy-five counties, including Huaiji, etc. In Hunan, it is sold in eleven counties, including Bixian, etc. In Jiangxi, it is sold in seventeen counties, including Ganxian, etc. In Fujian, it is sold in eight counties, including Changting, etc. In Guizhou, it is sold in ten counties, including Libo, etc. Only Jinping County in Guizhou Province sells both Huai salt and Guangdong salt. As for the transportation and sales methods, they are contracted by specialized merchants, with a monthly sales quota of a certain amount. For example, in Guangzhou, Hongtai Company contracts to sell 217,000 dan per month. Transport merchants are further divided into upper and lower river merchants. Lower river transport merchants can go to the salt fields to transport salt and return to the province to obtain allocations. Upper river transport merchants are solely responsible for transportation and sales. All contracting merchants who request the release of salt must obtain a tax payment slip from the local audit office, pay the tax at the Central Bank, and after the bank stamps it to prove receipt, bring it back to the audit agency that issued the slip to obtain a salt release permit. Then, they bring the permit to the Transport Commissioner's Office to affix the official seal and obtain a transport license. Only after all procedures are completed is it considered satisfactory. As for the monthly contracted quota, it can be paid in installments, but most have already borrowed several months' quota in advance.

The previous section described that the administrative and auditing parts of the Guangdong salt affairs system are still independent, and their powers are not intermingled. All matters such as issuing transport licenses, managing salt fields, and suppressing smuggling are handled by the Liangguang Salt Transport Commissioner's Office. All matters such as collecting salt taxes, issuing salt release permits, weighing and releasing salt, compiling summary reports of salt taxes, and repaying foreign debts related to salt affairs are the responsibility of the Guangdong Salt Affairs Audit Sub-office.

According to the index of the twentieth year of the Republic (1931), the income from Guangdong salt tax accounts for about one-tenth of the total annual salt tax revenue of the country, amounting to more than ten million national currency. The categories of taxes are also very numerous. Broadly speaking, they are divided into national and provincial taxes. Those belonging to national taxes include three items: regular tax, foreign debt surtax, and miscellaneous taxes. Such as assigned taxes, surcharge on field and road transport tax, fishery salt tax, and private salt supplementary tax, all belong to the regular tax. Water transport fees, allocation fees, salt permit fees for material boats, salt permit fees for fishing boats, salt rations, contracted rations, confiscation of private salt, price of fines, miscellaneous donations, fishing water donations, Min salt transport Shantou transit duty, and Min salt transport Shantou surcharge belong to the miscellaneous taxes. As for the provincial tax, there was previously a 20% Central Paper Currency Surtax, which has now been discontinued. Currently, there is a surcharge for purchasing anti-smuggling ships. In Shantou, there was previously the Chao-Mei River Governance Donation, which has now been changed to the Bandit Suppression Donation. As for annual expenditures, in addition to monthly allocations for administrative, anti-smuggling, and auditing expenses, it is also necessary to remit and repay foreign debt installments. The remaining tax revenue, except for the purchase of ship surcharge under the provincial tax item, is sent to the Liangguang Salt Transport Commissioner's Office for safekeeping, and the Bandit Suppression Donation is handed over to the Eastern District Pacification Commissioner's Office for use. The total is remitted to the Finance Special Commissioner's Office and transferred to the Guangdong Province for all military and political expenses.

The tax rate in Guangdong Province is 2.5 yuan in silver per dan for regular tax, 0.3 yuan in silver for foreign debt surtax, and an additional provincial tax. Salt permit fees for material boats and fishing boats are collected in grades, each with a fixed amount. Other taxes are also the same.

The accounting system of the Guangdong Salt Affairs Audit Department was divided into two major periods from July 1, 1931. In the previous period, the so-called financial accounts were merely the preparation of a report. There was no fixed accounting system or books for reference at any time. At the beginning of the establishment of the audit office, it adopted the old-fashioned accounts used by the customs. On July 1 last year, the audit office promoted the new accounting system of Dr. F. A. Cleveland (currently the director of the audit head office), which brought about a major reform in the accounts. It has been implemented for only one and a half years, and the results are remarkable, which is very commendable. It is necessary to praise the efforts of Dr. Cleveland and the audit chief in their efforts to rectify the situation. The key point of the accounting system lies in the independence of the three parts of the cashiers, accounting and auditing, so that internal checks and balances can be achieved and fraud can be reduced. This is what Dr. Cleveland intended to achieve by promoting the new accounting system. As for the preparation of other accounts, books, and reports, they are all very precise. Accounting comrades who love accounting, why not come and do a detailed study?

The above description of the salt affairs in Guangdong is only a bird's-eye view. It is inevitable that there will be omissions. It is a brief account of what the author can recall. I hope that readers will correct me. (Hongyi)

A Simple Explanation of Modern Currency (3) 153

— Translated by Ke

Chapter 2: The Standard of Currency

From this point of view, under this system, the price of gold and silver has a certain standard. However, this situation can also be expressed in another way, that is, the price of coins is fixed. Each coin can be exchanged for a certain amount of gold or silver. (Note 1)

In this situation, there is a crucial point contained within, and this point is the source of all difficulties. Under the bimetallic standard, the transaction price of gold and silver is stipulated by the government by law. Once this ratio is determined, it is extremely difficult to change it, and it always causes various financial and commercial disorders. The statutory ratio between gold and silver is somewhat arbitrary. Although it can sometimes reflect the comparative value of the two, it can only match for a very short period of time and cannot remain unchanged for a long time. The reason for this is that gold and silver are also commodities, just like rice, wheat, and leather. The value between the two is often fluctuating. Let us assume that on the day the order is issued, the transaction value of gold and silver is under the formula of supply and demand, labor, and transportation costs, and the ratio is one to sixteen. Therefore, the price ratio of gold and silver is set at one to sixteen. But on the second day, a new gold mine is suddenly discovered, and we can obtain a large amount of gold at a lower cost. At the same time, a large silver mine is flooded and cannot be produced. In addition, a new industry is booming and requires a large amount of raw silver. As a result, gold is flooded and silver is scarce. If there is an open market for gold and silver, the price ratio between the two will change immediately. The price of gold will fall and the price of silver will rise. The ratio of the value of the two must not stop at the flat line of sixteen to one.

In recent decades, the production of silver has increased greatly, on the one hand due to the development of new silver mines, and on the other hand due to the advancement of metallurgy, which has enabled a large amount of pure silver to be extracted from other metals. Therefore, the supply of pure silver far exceeds its demand, and its price has also fallen sharply. On the other hand, in terms of gold, experts are always worried about its scarcity and fear that it will be insufficient for use. Although there is no lack of杞人憂天, its price has already risen sharply.

We have said above that if there is an open market for gold and silver, the rise and fall of its price will be the same as the rise and fall of the price of other goods, that is, it is determined by the supply and demand. In countries with a bimetallic standard, there is no such open market for gold and silver. The government always buys or sells gold and silver at a fixed price at any time. However, although an open market for gold and silver cannot be obtained in countries with a bimetallic standard, it can always be obtained internationally. The world has not been united into one, and abides by a common gold and silver price ratio. In each country, the gold and silver price ratio is different. Sometimes, countries with a single standard also buy and sell a metal that is not legal tender as an ordinary commodity at will. As a result, the gold and silver price ratio is disordered, and the drawbacks of the bimetallic standard system are rampant.

After any country adopts the bimetallic standard, after a considerable period of time, one of the currencies of that country will be swept away to foreign countries. This loss can destroy the progress of commerce, reduce the amount of import and export trade, impoverish the public, and create general confusion.

Why will one of the currencies of that country be swept away to foreign countries? A little observation will show that the reason is very simple. According to economic principles, commodities flow to the market with the highest price. Therefore, countries with high gold prices gain gold and lose silver, and countries with high silver prices lose gold and gain silver. The circulation between them cannot be stopped by any law or power. Because people are willing to take risks to seek profit, and there is great profit in the circulation of gold and silver. Therefore, even if there is a legal prohibition, they will still tend to it regardless.

This situation can be illustrated by an example. In 1798, the United States, through the efforts of Alexander Hamilton, adopted the bimetallic standard through Congress, stipulating that one ounce of pure gold could be exchanged for fifteen ounces of pure silver. Later, France set the price ratio of gold and silver at fifteen and a half to one. As a result, American gold flowed to France, and French silver flooded the American market. In 1834, the US government changed the price ratio of gold and silver to sixteen to one. As a result, all the silver in the American market flowed to other countries with higher silver prices and disappeared. The same situation also occurred in England.

What is the lesson of this situation? What is the difference between exchanging gold for silver and exchanging silver for gold? A little deeper investigation will show that there are many difficulties. Now, let us give one example to illustrate the rest. Under this situation, a country cannot regulate the amount of currency circulating in the market. The reason for this is about three points: ㈠ Exchanging gold for silver may be equal in value and quantity, but the gold and silver obtained are the currency or bullion of foreign countries. Therefore, it must be recast before it can circulate in the market. ㈡ The entry and exit of currency are delayed for a long time in transit, so no one can know the exact number of all at one time. ㈢ Sometimes the price of one currency is greater than the price of another currency. All of this makes the supply of currency fluctuate and its quality changes from time to time. As a result, Gresham's Law takes effect, good money flows out and bad money floods in, all prices change accordingly, and the economic stability is destroyed.

Moreover, it is also very inconvenient in fact for a country to adopt one kind of coin as the standard and use other kinds of coins for supply.

There are many such difficulties. Now, I will not describe them one by one. But this does not mean that the theory of the bimetallic standard is a fallacy, nor does it mean that this system cannot run smoothly under the international unified gold and silver price ratio. In fact, the bimetallic standard system has had good results in France, and it has also run smoothly in the later Latin Monetary Union (including France, Italy, Belgium, Switzerland, and Greece).

The theory of those who advocate the bimetallic standard system is roughly as follows:

If gold and silver are both coined into legal tender and can be used interchangeably, the market's demand for currency will cause the two to circulate in the market in a considerable ratio of quantity. Although these two are commodities with different industrial or other uses, their influence is not enough to shift the ratio of the quantity of their circulation. (To be continued)

Free Talk

Miss Swallow (2)

— Ye Feng

She led me to a small room on the third floor of a building facing the street on Old Target Road (老靶子路). She said it was her temporary residence, where she had been living for five days.

"It's where my friend Marie lives. Marie works as a hostess at the Blue Flower Coffee Shop. She's a friend I made in the Philippines. Today she went to the Pik Huang Kek (辟克惶克) in Nanxiang. I only know her in Shanghai."

Looking at the single iron bed, the half-drawn curtain, the small Irish pottery pot, and the open-lidded Coddy flour, I felt that this was like a made-up image of my own bedroom, the homeless home of a wandering soul.

"So, you're living here alone. What are you going to do?"

Having read novels for half my life and wandered for half my life, I'm used to thinking about things that aren't my own.

"Look, this is him. He's the one who asked me to come."

She opened a box in the corner of the room that wasn't locked. Without looking, she skillfully pulled out a photo, came over, and stood next to me.

It was a photo of a middle-aged man with a large face, thick eyebrows, and a wide mouth, but with two sad little eyes.

The lower corner of the photo was scrawled with...

ToMyLitterSwallow

Below that was a signature that was hard to recognize.

"Is this your name?" I asked.

"They always like to call me that."

"What does he do in Shanghai?"

She smiled, as if she was apologizing for her friend's disreputable occupation.

"He used to be an assistant at a sailor's bar in the Philippines. Now he's in Shanghai doing... I don't know what he's doing now."

"Have you known each other for a long time?"

She opened her handbag, took out two long cigarettes, put one in her own mouth, and offered one to me.

I shook my head.

"Not now."

She threw the cigarette she had offered me on the bed, lit a match, lit the cigarette in her own mouth, took a puff, and blew out a smoke ring.

"You men are always like that. You want something when you need it, and you shake your head when you don't. I've known him for three years, and he's left me six times. He gets cheated by other people and then comes back to me. He forgets about the other people and runs off to them again. I've followed him from the Philippines to Honolulu, from Honolulu to Macau, and from Macau back to the Philippines. This is the second time I've been to Shanghai. Following him, like spring, I'm living the life of a swallow."

She sighed slightly, looked at the sky outside the window, took a puff of her cigarette, and slowly blew out the smoke that she had inhaled, with her head tilted back.

"I'm not like that," I said. "She left with someone else and never came back. I've been waiting for several springs."

"But," she said, as if comforting me and herself, "I believe he will definitely come back. She will definitely come back too. Don't you think so?"

I no longer believed it, but I had to say...

"Yes, I believe she will definitely come back."

For the first time, a smile appeared on her small face.

The Outer Strength and Inner Weakness of Men of Letters 159

— Ms. Luyin

Indeed, to bear the signboard of a man of letters on one's shoulders, one must at least be unrestrained beyond the confines of social norms. The most admirable thing is to take money lightly, as if selling one's trousers to visit a prostitute were the epitome of a carefree life. Originally, the Tang Dynasty poet Li Bai was the best example for men of letters—the so-called "Five-flower horse, thousand-gold fur, call the boy to exchange them for fine wine, to dispel with you the sorrow of ten thousand ages!" And also, "A thousand gold spent, will return again!" Such romantic and extravagant behavior is much to be envied, so it's no wonder that contemporary men of letters are always talking about how they don't care about money.

Although men of letters take money very lightly, everyone else—such as the rice store owner and the coal store boss—won't do business without it. This really puts men of letters in a difficult position. In public, men of letters treat money like dirt, but deep down, they deeply understand its power and oppression. Therefore, this discord between their inner and outer selves leads to various contradictory outcomes—

············

One fine afternoon, a group of casually dressed men of letters gathered around a rectangular dining table.

Whiskey, "San Pao Tai" liquor, toast, and beer piled up on the table, and the men of letters, feeling right at home, indulged themselves beyond the bounds of propriety. One bottle, one cup, what a heroic drinking session!

Soon, the sun set, and one of the men of letters, Mr. You, stood up and said, "It's time for us to leave!" The waiter had already prepared the bill and presented it respectfully on a small tray. Mr. You took it and saw that it was thirty dollars and five cents. He generously took a wad of bills from his wallet and quietly counted out thirty-one dollars and two cents. He handed the thirty-one dollars to the waiter, intending to say, "Keep the change," but then he thought of his wife waiting at home to buy candy for the children. So, he quickly swallowed a mouthful of saliva and said, "Bring back the change." The waiter grunted and left, returning with five cents. Mr. You took the two small coins he had left in his pocket and put them on the tray, keeping the five-cent piece in his wallet. The waiter sneered and spat, muttering as they walked out, "What kind of 'Chilao' is pretending to be a big spender?" Mr. You only shrugged his shoulders, acting as if he didn't care.

Mr. You returned home, and his wife rushed out to meet him, saying, "Hey, what are you going to do? The landlord sent someone to urge us to pay the rent again. He said we haven't paid rent for three months, and if we don't come up with something soon, he'll have to ask us to move out."

Mr. You said "Oh" and raised his right hand to scratch his head, calculating in his mind: "When it comes to making money, my skills aren't bad. As long as there's a loophole to exploit, I'll exploit it. This month, I managed to get three hundred dollars, but I haven't been feeling well and need to eat some nourishing tonics. The soft-shelled turtle at Nanxing Residence cost me over a hundred dollars every day. And then there's that pretty girl, Ah Lan, who squeezed me for over a hundred dollars. Alas, I'm really cursed! I could have made a small fortune, but I ran into that enemy of mine, Zhang, who wants to audit the bookstore's accounts. Otherwise, I could have kept at least one-third of the printing money to help with the emergency!"

Seeing him lost in thought and silent, his wife couldn't help but explode, "What exactly are you planning? Are you just going to ignore it?"

"Don't worry, what's the big deal? Can't a famous writer like me support you? You women are always so petty."

"Stop bragging, what do you men of letters have besides your mouths? ... I usually try to reason with you, but you're always saying that men of letters don't care about money, and that you are great. Let's see how great you are now, I really don't understand, how much does greatness sell for a pound? ..." As she spoke, his wife couldn't help but chuckle. Mr. You seized the opportunity to step down, respectfully bowing to his wife and saying, "Okay, Madam!"

"Don't put on that act with me, I see right through you!"

"What do you see through me?"

"I see through you, hmph, a pretentious and useless man of letters with outer strength but inner weakness."

"Well said! Well said!" Mr. You scratched the back of his head, swallowed his saliva, and continued to be tolerant.

Christmas Gifts 160

— Ms. Wang

In a clever, beautiful, floral box, there was a red Santa Claus and three singing birds. Sister Qi braved the winter cold to bring me this gift from afar.

At night, amidst the fatigue of work, surrounded by a group of strangers, after uttering meaningless greetings, my mind clouded, carrying a lonely heart, I quietly walked back from the noisy crowd.

The room was lonely.

I pushed open the glass window, looked up at the sky, and the stars shone with clear brilliance. I took a slight breath and turned around. On the table stood Santa Claus, holding a gauze bag in one hand and a holly branch in the other, with a snow-white beard, smiling at me. It suddenly reminded me that it was the Christmas season! But I smiled sadly.

In dreamlike, hazy memories, I recalled the innocent, joyful childhood and the blurred, lovely image of my mother.

Time flowed like water, and ten years passed quickly.

At that time, like other happy children, I had a kind and gentle mother, and a happy family—

When I was little, the happiest and most welcome time was the New Year, but because my mother was a devout Christian, the impression of Christmas was deeply etched in my mind.

Every Christian family was busy with celebratory ceremonies, and my family was the same. My father would start buying holly trees, shiny silver tinsel, red and white candles, Santa Claus, and many other fun things ten days in advance. My mother was busy knitting woolen outerwear and making flower shoes for me, and teaching me to sing "Silent Night" while playing the piano in the evening.

On Christmas Eve, the large Christmas tree, which had taken several days to decorate, was placed in the center of the room. The floor was covered with snowflake-like white paper, and large, bright candles were lit on the table, along with many red and white candles on the Christmas tree, creating a humorous and peaceful glow, scattered on the oily green walls. The stove was burning with red flames. I changed into new clothes, wondering what Christmas gifts my father and mother would give me. My mother quietly played the piano, and the song "Silent Night" echoed in the deep night.

Our hearts leaped with joyful extravagance.

When I was just ten years old, my mother abandoned me and left this dark world forever!

Time flowed like water, and ten years passed quickly.

However, sometimes, when these sad memories were evoked, I would feel overwhelmed with distress. I used strong willpower to suppress my tears, and I would run alone to the cemetery, to the side of the railroad tracks, and silently pour out my sorrow in the depths of my soul to the sky, to the withered old trees.

I thought about how my mother had loved me, and how many precious sacrifices she had made to make me a "true person" in this world. I also repeatedly thought of the happy home of my childhood.

Tonight, amidst the fatigue of work, surrounded by a group of strangers, after uttering meaningless greetings, my mind clouded, carrying a lonely heart, I quietly walked back from the noisy crowd.

The room was lonely.

The red Santa Claus was smiling at me, but I burst into tears of sadness!

Great Men and "Death" 162

— Zhao Jiabi

Death is the end of life, and the last words spoken from the bottom of their hearts by many great souls as they bid farewell to the world of the living are worth remembering by those of us who are still alive at this moment.

The Greeks viewed death as nothing more than an ordinary event. Life is like a growing tree, and when the fruit is ripe, it must go to another world. Therefore, death is as commonplace as "going to sleep at the end of a happy day." Socrates, on his deathbed, told those who were seeing him off, "My friends, I still owe Asclepius a rooster!" The Greek biographer Diogenes, when a friend asked him, "Who will bury your body?" He said, "Whoever buys my house will have to bury me."

In France, there used to be a saying, "to die without saying a word," but great French figures always had something to say on their deathbeds. Rabelais said, "It is finished, my feet that have walked the long road have brought me here." Ronsard said, "Farewell, my dear friends, I will go ahead and prepare a place." As for the heroes of the French Revolution, there are even more precious last words.

Many words were spoken on the guillotine. Peletier trembled when he saw the guillotine, and the spectators shouted, "Are you afraid to die?" He said, "No, I feel cold!" But when he was refused by the executioner and was not allowed to embrace his friend who was to be executed at the same time, he said bitterly, "Damn you, you can't stop our heads from kissing in the basket!" Because after the execution, the heads were put together in a basket. These heroes' last words can be compared to those of Chinese revolutionary heroes who, at the execution ground, loudly proclaimed, "In twenty years, I will be a good man again!" Both are admirable.

Among many modern literary figures, some last words are also worth noting. The French poet Musset said, "How troublesome a thing death is!" Because he died young, but in his short life he had suffered enough from love and pain. When Renan died, he said, "It is God, the sun is calling me! God has opened the door of my chest." When the German poet Heine was dying, a pastor was praying to God to ask "him" to forgive, Heine said, "Why ask? That is 'his' job!" The French poet Vigny said to God on his deathbed, "The final judgment will come on the day God asks mankind for forgiveness for creating mankind."

The Late Poet Han Shibo 163

— Ping

Mr. Han Shibo was a native of Dantu, Jiangsu. He studied under Zhang Jian of Tongzhou in his youth, but his talent was overflowing and radiant, yet he was incompatible with Mr. Zhang Si. His poems, especially his quatrains, are truly rare since the Tang and Song dynasties. If I say this, some people will say that I am short-sighted and that I am exaggerating, but let's see what his poems are really like.

Lamenting Layman Yang Renshan:

Dressed in grass, sitting on a tiger at the city wall, the wind circles the cattail cushion for ten thousand autumns. To speak of the old Layman Yang Renshan, heaven and earth shook as he entered Nirvana.

Layman Yang Renshan was a great master of Chinese Buddhism. When the Xinhai Revolution broke out, the layman happened to be in Nanjing, inviting great Buddhist scholars to entrust them with his robe and bowl, and then he returned to the Dao and passed away. The poem is probably a factual record.

Moonlit Night Climbing Anqing City - A Quatrain:

A pagoda suddenly rides the river, the city's shade is cool, the moon is white and scattered. Ling Lake wants to swallow the dragon's tail, petals of lotus enter the clouds at night!

Let's take the latter poem as an example. The first line breaks through the void and arrives, like Mount Tai flying over, blocking the way, but it is a factual record, not the poet's fantasy, which is its first wonderful aspect. The second line is very difficult to follow. One would think that it must be a majestic and慷慨 sentence, so as not to "place dung on the Buddha's head," but the reply "the city's shade is cool, the moon is white and scattered" is another imaginative idea, taking the entire calm world of a moonlit night into view, which is so beautiful! This is its second wonderful aspect. The third line suddenly makes a bold and fearless imagination, corresponding to the first line, and the fourth line enters a cool world, ethereal and wanting to become an immortal, and the author's great imagination and great personality are transformed into it. This is its third wonderful aspect. However, if you only compare it with the poems of poets such as Su Manshu, then it is simply worlds apart. Shibo's poems are not only majestic in sound and rhyme, but also have the color and light of ascending the Great Buddha Hall. As for his fraternity and active spirit, they are unparalleled in the world. Most of the quatrains since the Tang and Song dynasties have focused their efforts on the latter two lines, but Lao Han's poems are like dragons rising and tigers taking hold from the beginning, and every word falls to the ground with the sound of gold and stone. This is why I cherish and introduce them.

The author also wants to advise old-style doctors. Even if you are enlightened, you must start anew, and never try to be novel. Therefore, I want to advise old-style doctors that if you truly understand science yourself, then you can organize old-style medicine. Then, you will also be a new-style doctor, and we will certainly welcome you very much. If you see the trend of the times and have your son study science, then your son will be a new-style doctor. Then, old-style medicine will naturally be organized using scientific methods, which is the same as the current trend of new-style doctors organizing old-style medicine. If you think there are too many doctors, then in the future, I will only let my little dog study other subjects, and there will be no traditional concept of making a living. It is necessary to use medicine to help the world. I have often compared it to a copper clepsydra and a grandfather clock. They are both things that measure time, and old-style and new-style doctors have the same goal of curing diseases. However, in terms of the times, the copper clepsydra is already too inaccurate. Therefore, we must use clocks and watches. Why only allow the shop of copper clepsydras to put glass frames on the clepsydras and pretend to be clocks and watches, and not allow engineers from clock and watch factories to go to the copper clepsydra shop to take materials to make clocks? It can be seen that it is public to create copper clocks and watches to adapt to the trend, and it is private to only create copper clepsydras in order to maintain the shop. Now, many of the articles written by old-style doctors have already acknowledged that bacteriology, anatomy, and other subjects cannot be erased, and that using X-rays to examine the internal organs has been included in the science of diagnosis. This is the effect of the loud cries of new-style doctors, and it is also admirable that old-style doctors are willing to follow good advice. However, when it comes to later, they often say something about "distinguishing meridians and identifying collaterals," and using "imagination and impression" to diagnose diseases, and gradually enter metaphysics again. This situation is not a characteristic of the old-style medical community, but of our country's education itself, which has not taken natural science seriously. The various medicines are described as follows.

Although the Doctors' Association was established in this new medical community, there are also some people who have not yet joined. The Psychology of the Sick 166

— Song Guobin

Chapter 1: General Introduction to Psychology

Section 1: Methods of Research

The condition of an illness varies with age, gender, temperament, and environment, differing in its development, prognosis, and treatment. Similarly, the psychology of a patient varies with age, gender, temperament, and environment in its tendencies. A physician should be skilled in observing and treating them differently. Therefore, one who is adept at analyzing the psychology of a patient is considered a good doctor. For only with a keen mind and dexterous skill can one adapt to changes and handle situations with ease. Insects rely on their antennae to avoid dangers ahead, while humans rely on their keen observation to solve all difficulties. The so-called keenness and dexterity, though received through heredity, can also be acquired through training. One who cannot analyze the psychology of others cannot practice medicine. After opening a practice, they will inevitably suffer spiritual and economic losses. If they have a special interest in medicine, they can only confine themselves to the laboratory and cannot set up a clinic.

To understand the psychology of a patient, it is essential to show empathy and goodwill to the patient, ensuring that the patient can fully express their feelings to the doctor. Only then can the doctor fully understand the patient's psychology. However, the patient's words should not be taken entirely at face value. Attention must also be paid to their actions, the manner of their speech, and the expressions on their face. By cross-referencing and studying these aspects, the analyzed psychology can be grounded in reality.

Students who pay attention to the above-mentioned tasks during their hospital internships will undoubtedly become good doctors in the future. There is no doubt about it.

Section 2: ㈠ Sources of Disagreement Between Doctors and Patients and Methods of Resolution

There are roughly four points of contention between doctors and patients:

㈠ Differences in Status: The status of doctors and patients is often divided into aristocratic and common. It is not difficult for a doctor of aristocratic background to treat a common patient in a common manner. However, if a doctor of common background treats an aristocratic patient, they often lose their composure. Therefore, during their school years, they must practice etiquette and speech to avoid vulgarity and cultivate a scholarly demeanor. In short, adapting to the environment is the key to practicing medicine. Only the doctor should defer to the patient, not the other way around.

㈡ Conflicts of Thought: Conflicts sometimes arise between patients and doctors when discussing social issues due to differences in their thinking. The only solution is to avoid discussing issues unrelated to the diagnosis and treatment of the illness altogether. Even if the patient speaks at length, the doctor should only respond with polite agreement and should not engage in debate. After all, a doctor should view the patient as a patient, and there is no need to conflict with their opinions.

㈢ Language Barriers: Different regions have different dialects. Doctors and patients often encounter difficulties due to language barriers. Therefore, a doctor opening a practice in a certain area must first learn the local language. Furthermore, patients have varying levels of education. Doctors must tailor their language, making it either refined or common, according to the patient's level of literacy.

㈣ Differences in Beliefs: Some patients with a superficial understanding of medical principles may presumptuously argue with the doctor's prescriptions and medications. Others, with stubborn minds, may express their admiration for traditional Chinese medicine in front of a modern doctor. These are all instances of differing beliefs. In such cases, the doctor should gently guide them and avoid extreme rejection. (To be continued)

Theory of Treatment (Continued) 167

— Yu Gong

㈤ Light Therapy: The use of sunlight and ultraviolet light to treat tuberculosis and radium to treat malignant tumors has remarkable results and occupies an important position among various treatment methods. The technique is highly specialized and cannot be fully understood by those with only a superficial understanding.

㈥ Mental Therapy: Some diseases arise from unfavorable environments, leading to depression and melancholy, causing mental decline. Once, a woman who was breastfeeding her child had scarce milk supply. She sought treatment from a doctor. The doctor observed the worry on her face and inquired about her family history. He learned that she was at odds with her mother-in-law, so he advised her to live separately. Soon, her milk supply increased, and the child's weight also increased. This shows that mental comfort is far more effective than medication. In the case of the aforementioned condition, relying on medication would not be effective, it can be stated with certainty.

To ensure the proper application of the above methods, sufficient academic knowledge, skillful techniques, rich experience, and adequate equipment are essential. Therefore, the strength of one doctor is often insufficient, so they consult with other doctors. Or the facilities of the outpatient clinic are inadequate, so the patient is sent to the hospital. If treating a disease is simply a matter of taking medication, then medicine is not so simple. Moreover, the so-called miracle drugs, such as quinine for malaria, Salvarsan for syphilis, and serum for diphtheria, are few in number. Other drugs can only treat the symptoms, not the cause. The relief of symptoms does not mean that the source of the disease is gone. For example, if one suffers from tonsillitis, "acetophenetidin" can be used to relieve the headache, but it cannot be said that "acetophenetidin" is a miracle drug for tonsillitis. Patients with diphtheria often suffer from pain and cannot sleep, so morphine or codeine can be used to calm them, but it cannot be said that morphine or codeine is a miracle drug for diphtheria. Patients with measles use benzoin steam to stop coughing, but it cannot be said that benzoin is a miracle drug for measles. Patients with tuberculosis use atropine to stop night sweats and dilute hydrochloric acid or gentian tincture to stimulate appetite, but it cannot be said that [dilute hydrochloric acid] or [gentian tincture] is a miracle drug for tuberculosis. Patients with nephritis use pilocarpine to induce sweating and magnesium sulfate to induce bowel movements, but it cannot be said that pilocarpine or magnesium sulfate is a miracle drug for nephritis. All of these involve using medication to treat the symptoms. However, the relief of symptoms can also be achieved by "non-pharmacological methods." Therefore, when seeking medical treatment, patients should be cautious not to regard medication as the only weapon against disease.

Common Knowledge Questions About Diseases 168

— Cheng Hanzhang

㈠ Scarlet Fever

Q: What is scarlet fever?

A: Scarlet fever is a highly contagious disease, commonly known as "rotten throat rash."

Q: What is the pathogen of scarlet fever?

A: Recent discoveries indicate that scarlet fever is caused by the transmission of a type of streptococcus, known as hemolytic streptococcus.

Q: How does this pathogen invade the human body?

A: It invades through the mucous membranes of the nasal passages and throat, or through the tonsils and pharyngeal lymph nodes. It can also invade through external wounds on the skin.

Q: At what age is this disease most easily transmitted?

A: It is most common in children between the ages of two and ten. It is less common in infants and adults.

Q: After infection with the scarlet fever bacteria, how long does it take for the disease to develop?

A: The incubation period is three to six days before the disease develops.

Q: What are the initial symptoms of the disease?

A: The initial symptoms include chills and shivering, a rapid rise in body temperature, and sometimes vomiting and convulsions. Soon after, neck problems develop, with difficulty swallowing, and swelling of the tonsils and soft palate.

Q: What happens later?

A: Later, on the second day, red rashes appear on the neck and upper chest, reaching their peak in three or four days and gradually spreading to the torso and limbs. However, rashes on the face are rare, and the area around the lips is completely free of red rashes, so it appears pale.

Q: What is the size and shape of these rashes?

A: Each rash is about the size of a pinhead. Initially, they are pale red spots, and the skin's surface can still be seen. Later, more rashes appear and merge into a single area, turning deep red, hence the name scarlet fever.

Q: On what day does the rash begin to fade?

A: By the tenth day, the temperature may return to normal.

Q: What does the tongue of a scarlet fever patient look like?

A: The mucous membrane of the tongue peels off and is also scarlet red and rough, resembling the texture of a bayberry or a cat's tongue.

Q: Why do most people with scarlet fever also suffer from a rotten throat?

A: Because pharyngitis occurs in conjunction with throat inflammation, leading to erosion.

Q: What other complications can occur during scarlet fever?

A: The most common complication is nephritis. The patient's urine contains protein, the body temperature rises again, the face becomes swollen, the whole body swells, there is ascites, the amount of urine decreases, and it contains blood. Eventually, uremia develops, which is very dangerous.

Q: Are there heart complications?

A: Yes, sometimes there are complications such as endocarditis, myocarditis, and pericarditis, as well as a rapid pulse.

Q: How does the skin return to its original state after the illness?

A: The skin affected by scarlet fever rashes peels off in large pieces.

Q: How should scarlet fever patients be treated?

A: They should rest quietly in bed, and the sickroom should be warm and humid. The diet should consist of liquids. The mouth should be rinsed frequently with hydrogen peroxide. Injections of cardiotonics and the administration of diuretics are also effective. Milk should be given when the patient is thirsty. Injections of scarlet fever serum are also very effective.

The Use of Traditional Chinese Medicine in Western Medicine (Continued) 169

— Zhou Mengbai

(1) Yellow Hollyhock Root (Abelmoschus)

Origin:

This product is a plant in the Malvaceae family, the fresh root of Abelmoschus Manibot. It is dug up, the cork removed and dried.

Shape:

This product is a root strip with a sharp, narrow lower end and slightly branched. The color is white, and it is rich in starch.

Its cross-section is also off-white. There are tangentially arranged fiber bundles in the cortex. The center has small dots.

Composition:

This product contains a lot of real mucus. Other ingredients include asparagine, starch, sugar, and acid salts.

Experiment:

Add one gram of this product to ten milliliters of distilled water, stir it from time to time, let it stand for half an hour and filter it. You get a light yellow mucus. The taste of this mucus must be bland, without acid gas or sub-gas. Adding a few drops of a light sodium hydroxide test solution should turn it dark yellow immediately.

Efficacy:

This product is a smooth drug. It is suitable for stomach, intestinal and throat inflammation. It is often used as a cold soak decoction. European hollyhock root (Padix Althae) can be used as a substitute for this product.

Contraindications:

This product loses its efficacy when combined with bismuth subnitrate. If it is not stored dry, it is easy to become moldy. When drying, a slight temperature should be applied. If the temperature is too high, it may appear yellow.

(Appendix: Old Sayings) The roots and stems treat painful urination. Decoction and taking it are miraculous. It also treats children's oral ulcers. In the case of those that have been rotten for many years, burn the hollyhock root, grind it into powder, and apply it. Its flowers, dried in the shade, treat women's vaginal discharge. The seedlings are sweet, slightly cold and slippery. They should not be eaten for a long time. They dull people's intelligence. (To be continued)

Our Country Urgently Needs to Manufacture New Drugs to Meet the Needs of Both Traditional and Modern Medicine 170

— Guang

Modern medicine has made rapid progress. The depth of its research and the greatness of its inventions are truly advancing at a rapid pace. This is because scientific medicine is based on experimentation and emphasizes accuracy. It does not engage in empty talk or lean towards idealism. It is committed to the truth, even unto death. Therefore, even the slightest evidence or the slightest efficacy of a drug, if it is truly proven, will be recognized and adopted by the whole world. Our country has been impacted by the new trends, and in recent years, it has gradually begun to emphasize scientific medicine. Those who go abroad to study are constantly on the road. Those who return with a wealth of knowledge are too numerous to count. As for public and private medical schools in the country, and medical schools established by foreigners, there are no less than several dozen. Each year, a number of new doctors are inevitably produced. The increasing number of new doctors is inevitable. However, all the medical drugs and equipment used by these new doctors are sourced from foreign countries. Suppose there are fifty thousand new doctors in the country, each spending five hundred yuan per year on new drugs, that would amount to two hundred and fifty million yuan. If there are one hundred thousand new doctors, then it would be fifty million yuan. If we calculate based on hospitals, the expenditure per hospital is ten times greater. The more new doctors there are, the greater the need. With such a huge amount of money flowing abroad, is it not a huge leakage? This is why it is urgent to manufacture new drugs to counteract this. Furthermore, new medicine is scientific medicine, world medicine. Its treatment of diseases is often based on a global perspective and on-site observation. Any scientific doubts or profound mysteries of diseases that need to be elucidated are thoroughly researched. If something is discovered, it is made public and disseminated so that the whole world can benefit from it and alleviate human suffering. There is no room for secrecy. Therefore, prescriptions are only for scientific drugs, only those with true and reliable effects are chosen, only the purest products are accepted, and only those that are absolutely harmless are included. It does not promote heresy or encourage empty words. Its standards are extremely strict. However, today's pharmaceutical factories take advantage of the weaknesses of the people and, while our country's drug laws have not yet been promulgated, often advertise their products without the adoption of doctors. Posters are pasted in the streets, and anyone can buy and take them. Patients, because of the appealing words and the suitability of the condition, are happy to try them, often sacrificing their lives. No wonder the people often criticize the deception of new drugs and ridicule the uselessness of new medicine. I know that if this continues, new drugs will lose their inherent value, and new doctors will indirectly lose their credibility. The future of science is fraught with danger. To correct this, we must establish large-scale chemical pharmaceutical factories, based on pure medical principles, to create completely scientific drugs, to overturn all foreign medicines, and to maintain the reputation of new drugs. This is why the manufacture of new drugs cannot be delayed. With our country's thousands of years of medical history, traditional Chinese medicine has used no less than a thousand kinds of drugs. Among them, there are many effective kinds. If we can select the most effective ones, analyze them chemically, and refine their pure forms, we will surely make a great contribution to the development of new medicine. For example, ephedra and angelica have already been adopted by the world and have become precedents. Those who shoulder this responsibility are only the domestic pharmaceutical factories. The identification is true, and the materials are easy to obtain. This is the third reason why it is urgent to manufacture new drugs. Moreover, our country has a vast territory and abundant resources. What place does not have the raw materials for manufacturing new drugs? Why must we buy them from foreign countries? What worries us is that there is no one to manufacture them and that the procurement is hesitant, so that goods are abandoned on the ground, without knowing how to use them. If there is a need, we have to rely on others. What a shame. At a time when gold is expensive and silver is cheap, foreign medicines, manufactured with extreme precision, are suitable for the use of new medicine, but their value is incredibly high. They can only be used by the wealthy class. As for the common people and small workers, the number of patients is the largest. When they hear about the price of new drugs, they shake their heads and click their tongues. They cannot afford to buy them. Even if they want to seek medical treatment, they dare not. The inability to make new medicine accessible is undeniable. If new drugs are manufactured domestically, wages will be low, costs will be lower, and they will not be affected by the price of gold, nor will they be monopolized by others. The price will naturally be lower. To make them accessible is easy. Therefore, for the convenience of new doctors, for the sake of accessibility, and for the benefit of patients, we must urgently manufacture new drugs and produce them in our own country. Only then can we truly promote the progress of new medicine.

My Philosophy of Life 171

— Xia Shenchu

Non-Resistance Leads to Extinction

We are surrounded by germs, lurking and waiting for an opportunity to expand their life lines. We have the city walls of skin, the moats of lymph nodes, and the warriors of white blood cells, resisting together to survive. Our lifelines, such as breathing and eating, like the respiratory and digestive systems, must communicate with the outside world to absorb nutrients. Naturally, there are also corresponding devices to prevent stealthy attacks. Therefore, germs that invade through the respiratory system trigger sneezing, coughing, and expectoration to expel them. If they invade through the digestive system, they trigger vomiting and diarrhea to expel them. This is the innate resistance mechanism and the essential element of human survival.

When we fail to take care of ourselves, germs seize the opportunity to enter, occupy key positions, and seize nutrients. This leads to the phenomenon of battle, known as disease, such as fever, which is a symbol of exerting resistance. If the resistance is insufficient, the body weakens day by day, and the germs rage, and the disease intensifies. If the resistance is victorious, the germs die, and the sick body recovers. Therefore, some diseases heal without medicine. In medicine, this is called the natural healing mechanism. The treatment of a good doctor primarily involves providing nutrition and drugs that are equivalent to weapons to the patient to support their resistance. If anything impairs their natural healing mechanism or inhibits their resistance, it is tantamount to helping the germs grow. This is what is meant by a quack doctor killing people.

If the patient does not use their natural healing mechanism, even good medicine is useless. Weapons are supplied to the warriors for continuous use, but they cannot fight on their own. Therefore, some diseases are not cured by any medicine, and good doctors are helpless.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

The Boundless Power of Buddhism 172

— Tian Fang

Reading the two special dispatches from Tokyo and Nanjing in this newspaper on the 20th of this month has made me, a religious rebel, deeply feel the boundless power of Buddhism. Now, let's reproduce these two special dispatches as follows:

Nanjing, Central News Agency, 19th: The Panchen Lama gave a banquet for reporters at the Overseas Chinese Reception Center at noon on the 19th. In his speech, the Panchen Lama said, "It has been almost ten years since I left Tibet. Fortunately, the conflict between Kham and Tibet has come to an end. I have always adhered to the principle of peace, traveling to Mongolia and the interior, promoting virtue and goodwill, hoping to use religious compassion to supplement what politics cannot achieve. Some say that I will use force to return to Tibet, but in reality, I have no such intention, nor do I have the strength. I sincerely hope that the Tibetan people will pledge allegiance to the central government to alleviate the worries about the west," and so on. Also, Tokyo, Telegraphic News Agency, 19th: The Abbot Otani Kōen of Higashi Honganji Temple, who recently returned to the sect after the bankruptcy problem was resolved, has decided to cross over to Manchuria to promote friendship between Japan and Manchuria through proselytization. He arrived in Beijing a day or two ago and has obtained the understanding of the military and foreign affairs authorities. It is expected to be realized in early January. Regarding this, the authorities of Higashi Honganji Temple told people the other day that it is a very good thing for the former abbot to cross over to Manchuria to reconcile Japan and Manchuria. Our sect is currently working hard to open up Manchuria, so we are very welcome. What a pair of compassionate monks! Although their actions are different, they both want to use religion to supplement what politics cannot achieve, which is no different. However, the "promoting virtue and goodwill" of the oriental monks seems to only be carried out domestically by the national monks, and they are still suspected of using "military force," which is more courageous and diligent. This has a lot to do with the place of origin. Originally, "lazy saints" were mostly produced in the tropics of India, because it is easy to make a living in the tropics. Most people do nothing all day long, so they often entertain themselves with fantasies, chewing on nonsense about thirty-three heavens and eighteen levels of hell, making astronomers and geologists gasp. However, once it crosses national borders, it starts a chemical reaction, merging with Taoism in China and taking on the flavor of "Bushido" in Japan. Although our "National Protection XX Master" - I can't remember the full title - also prayed for peace and the extension of national fortune, it seems that using magic before guns is not as effective as the oriental monks using it after guns. Although Japanese Buddhism was transmitted from China, in this regard, it is "blue surpassing blue." Our "National Master" is a bit ashamed. What I have said above is all nonsense. I only praise "the boundless power of Buddhism, granting all requests," "aggression" and "resistance" are accounted for in one hand, and things are a bit comical. Reading the Shurangama Sutra says, "All sentient beings are like hundreds of mosquitoes gathered in a container, buzzing and making a frenzy." My Buddha is divine, and he must also regret chewing his tongue during his lifetime, and after death - the Buddha said "Nirvana" - he is merely a human puppet. Let me declare that this has nothing to do with me!

Corrigendum: In "A Few Words to Mr. Da Yi" in yesterday's issue of this newspaper, "Why is all literature so good?" It should have been "Why is the new literature so good?" It was discovered that the word "new" was dropped by a worker and was not proofread, resulting in only a question without an answer, almost making it incoherent. We hereby make the correction.
