The Terrifying Green Gas 173

— Leng Mei

At the mention of "green gas," I imagine everyone would exhale and say, "What a fearsome thing!" Indeed, it is a highly toxic gas. Even inhaling a small amount can cause unpleasant sensations, and inhaling too much means signing your name on the ghost registry.

During the World War, poison gas artillery and various poison gas bombs all contained green gas. Countless lives were sacrificed to this inhumane weapon. To this day, the horrifying and tragic images remain deeply imprinted in our minds.

The reason for green gas's extreme toxicity is likely because, upon inhalation, it combines with the water in the lungs to form hydrochloric acid. This hydrochloric acid can corrode the lungs, leading to respiratory arrest and death.

Green gas is a yellowish-green gas with a peculiar and pungent odor that irritates the throat and nose. It is also highly toxic, approximately 2.5 times heavier than air. Under normal temperatures and pressures, one volume of clean water can dissolve 2.5 volumes of green gas, and this solution is called chlorine water.

In nature, there is no free chlorine element because its activity is extremely strong and it easily combines with other elements. Therefore, its compounds are abundant on Earth. Surprisingly, the table salt indispensable in our daily lives is a compound of highly toxic green gas and sodium (chemically known as Sodium Chloride). Jokingly speaking, if you were to give someone those two things separately, they probably couldn't handle it. However, if our dishes are lacking table salt, we are likely to throw a fit!

Green gas is indeed a poisonous substance, but its uses are very broad. It has a powerful bleaching effect. When moist colored cloth encounters this gas, it immediately fades. However, dry colored cloth shows no change. This shows that the bleaching action of green gas is not direct, but rather it first decomposes water to release oxygen. This nascent oxygen has extremely strong activity and oxidizes colored substances, causing them to fade. Green gas also has a significant sterilizing power, so it can be used as a disinfectant. The amount of chlorine used for the above two purposes is extremely large. Because it is inconvenient to transport, it is often manufactured into bleaching powder for industrial use.

Because chlorine gas has a wide range of uses, a large quantity of chlorine is manufactured in industry, usually directly from its compounds. Several methods are described below:

Electrolysis Process

When an electric current is passed through a solution of table salt, potassium chloride, or hydrochloric acid, these compounds decompose, and chlorine gas is released at the anode.

2NaCl＋H2O＝2NaOH＋H2＋Cl2

Deaconsprocess

Heat hydrochloric acid to a high temperature and combine it with oxygen from the air, and a portion of chlorine gas will be released.

4HCl＋O2＝2H2O＋2Cl2

However, this method requires a chloride, such as copper dichloride (CuCl2), as a catalyst to initiate the reaction. If copper dichloride is strongly heated, it will transform into copper dichloride (Cu2Cl2) and release some chlorine. 2CuCl2＝Cu2Cl2＋Cl2

At the same time, when copper dichloride encounters oxygen, it turns into copper dichloride oxide (Cu2OCl2).

2Cu2Cl2＋O2＋2Cu2ocL2

This copper dichloride oxide reacts with hydrochloric acid, turning back into copper dichloride and water. Cu2OCl2＋2HCl＋2CuCl2＋H2O

Thus, a cycle is formed, and a small amount of copper dichloride can be continuously used.

PechineyWeldonprocess

This method is quite valuable in industry.

When a solution of magnesium chloride (MgO) and magnesium chloride (MgCl2) is heated to a high temperature, it transforms into magnesium dichloride oxide (Mg2ICl2). Further heating produces hydrochloric acid and chlorine. The hydrogen in the hydrochloric acid comes from the water,

and the chlorine is displaced from the magnesium chloride by oxygen from the air. This mixture of gases can be passed through water to remove the hydrochloric acid, releasing chlorine. The magnesium oxide is not changed and can continue to be used.

When producing chlorine in the laboratory, the most common method is to heat manganese dioxide and concentrated hydrochloric acid together, which releases chlorine gas.

MnO2＋4HCl＝MnCl2＋H2O＋Cl2

Alternatively, dilute hydrochloric acid can be added to bleaching powder (caocl2) without heating, which also releases chlorine gas.

CaOCl2＋2HCl＝H2O＋CaCl2＋

Cl2

Chlorine gas can directly combine with various metals, such as sodium and antimony. (These metals can burn in chlorine gas and directly combine with it to form chlorides.) 2Na＋Cl2＝　　2NaCl

2Sb＋3Cl2＝2sBCl32Sb＋5Cl2＝2

SbCl5

If a mixture of chlorine and hydrogen gas is exposed to sunlight, a violent explosion will occur, forming oxygen chloride. The same result occurs when a burning candle is inserted into this gas mixture.

Phosgene, used in the Great War, is even more toxic than green gas and is also a chlorine compound. Chemically known as carbonyl chloride (COCL2), it can be produced by mixing chlorine gas and carbon monoxide and exposing it to sunlight. It is a volatile liquid with a boiling point of eighty-two degrees.

The reaction of chlorine with water is very important and is the principle behind the bleaching action of chlorine water. When chlorine gas is bubbled into water, two types of acids are formed: hydrochloric acid and hypochlorous acid.

Cl2＋H2O＝HCl＋ClO

Hypochlorous acid is extremely unstable and decomposes rapidly in sunlight.

2HClO＝2HCl＋O2

The nascent oxygen produced by this reaction has the function of bleaching. Chlorine can combine with nonmetals. For example, phosphorus can burn in chlorine gas, producing phosphorus trichloride (PCl2) vapor. Sulfur, when heated, can also slowly combine with it, forming sulfur dichloride (S2Cl2), which can be used to make sulfur-containing rubber. Although carbon does not easily combine directly with chlorine, several carbon-chlorine compounds produced indirectly are extremely important and have a wide range of uses, such as dichloromethane CHCl3 (Chloroform) and carbon tetrachloride CCl4.

The Kerosene Lamp 174

— Ling He

When the pugs were so hot they were sticking their tongues out, I, unable to bear the harassment of the Nanjing bugs (the Japanese bedbugs), moved to this desolate countryside. I live in a newly built house, and of course, there are no Nanjing bugs here. So I couldn't help but put my hand to my forehead and celebrate peace on earth.

This is a new village that hasn't been built for long. After a great fire not long ago, everything here turned to ashes and needed to be rebuilt. There is no running water, no gas, and no electric lights. So we, a poor couple, personally dug a well to replace running water, cut wild

Page 18

grass to replace gas, and burned kerosene to replace electric lights.

We are pitifully weak, and ashamed of our lack of construction ability, but we are also content because we can live peacefully from now on. What more could we ask for?

Late at night, I lean on the table and read. Whenever the kerosene is about to run out and the light becomes dim, I close my eyes and meditate, leaning back in the chair, my hands on my knees, mocking myself for being immersed in the dark, stagnant air.

Last night, two friends happened to come. One was neatly dressed in a Western suit, elegant and refined, and the other wore a long robe and sleeves, with a few oil stains splashed on his chest. But I treated them both with respect, personally taking out Fairy brand cigarettes from the White Dragon cigarette holder and offering them, even bending over to light their matches. Because I was deeply honored to be able to invite friends to visit such a simple residence.

But I worried that my friends would be dissatisfied with my dim kerosene lamp, because it was somewhat incompatible with their tastes. Sure enough, the friend in the Western suit opened his mouth: "Why did you move to a place that doesn't even have electric lights?"

"Uh..." I felt restless.

"This is so stuffy."

"Uh," I could only stammer. What else could I say?

"But it doesn't matter," the other friend opened his mouth, and I knew there was a slight turning point, I was saved.

"What does it matter?" he repeated, "As long as you can see, that's enough. Why do you have to have electric lights?"

"But..." The friend in the Western suit wanted to say more, but because I had drunk too much boiled water that day, I couldn't hold it in and ran to the back of the house to urinate. When I came back, I no longer heard them talking about the kerosene lamp. Really, I was saved.

Please Sit and Other Things 175

— Wen Bing

...Essays from a Tiny Room...

Please Sit: Generally, those who champion humanitarianism regard sitting in a rickshaw as the most inhumane thing. Indeed, one person pulls another; the one sitting is comfortable, and the one pulling suffers. But I think in today's society, since this system exists, rather than wearing a humanitarian mask and not sitting, which would leave them without a livelihood, it is better to take off the mask, suppress your conscience, and sit within your means, so that they can earn enough for half a liter of rice each day to fill their bellies. It is said that the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway has a fast train that arrives at the North Station every night at eleven o'clock. Around seven or eight o'clock, rickshaws from all over gather near the station. One night, it was already past eleven o'clock, and I was returning from a friend's house, passing through Boundary Road. I saw many rickshaws still parked on both sides of the road, clearly proving that the fast train was delayed. Their yawns, sighs, and groans blended together, and the firefly-like oil lamps seemed to be smiling sadly at their owners, the rickshaw pullers. I was walking shivering when a rickshaw suddenly emerged from the right side of the road. The puller bowed deeply to me and pleaded, "Please sit, give me a few coppers, the train is delayed, and I haven't seen any congee all day!" As he spoke, he actually knelt down with tears in his eyes. At that moment, I was so embarrassed that I couldn't walk or stand. Frantically, I rummaged through my pockets and gave him the only five coppers I had, saying, "I can't help it either, although I seem to be a little better off than you!" As I walked away, it seemed like I could still hear the voice, "Please sit, give me a few coppers..."!

The Words of a Famous Professor: After the September 18th Incident broke out, a famous professor in Shanghai published an article in XX magazine, saying, "The Japanese are really overestimating themselves. You must know that China is so big. Even if we lose the Northeast, we are still a big country and can still become strong." This is indeed a famous saying of the professor. China is indeed not small; it used to have twenty-one provinces, and now it has even more. But I think even if it is big, it is just a combination of a few pieces of land the size of the Northeast. If, as the famous professor said, losing the Northeast still makes us a big country, then losing the Yellow River and Tianjin will still make us a big country, and even if all eighteen provinces of the mainland are lost and all four hundred million compatriots are moved to the Pamirs, we will still not be small. Alas, our famous professor, our famous professor's immortal words!

A Wonderful Couplet: Recently, a wonderful couplet was discovered at the entrance of XX College:

Education, education

Students, students

Yes, we know very well that XX College is worthy of being called a "wild chicken" institution, supported by several frustrated politicians (trustees), with a successful politician as the president, and several fourth- or fifth-rate officials who have reached the end of their road as professors. There is also a group of children of officials who are loaded with money dyed with the blood and sweat of ordinary people to play the role of students, so the college looks like a college. Regarding "love," I heard that there are indeed achievements. Professors advocate from above, and students follow below, so the atmosphere of "love" fills the entire college, which is exactly what the wonderful couplet at the entrance says. I only deeply sigh that if the children they produce are still like the old types, then the bureaucratization of China has the hope of continuing forever. Alas, how brilliant!

A Strange Phenomenon 176

— Yu Cheng

A Gen had been doing business in Shanghai for several years, and it seemed like he had been skinned alive. His attitude was completely different from before. A half-new serge suit, a pair of shiny leather shoes, a striped cloth shirt, and a red satin tie scared and envied all the mud-legged people in his hometown.

"Shanghai is said to be a fairyland. What is it really like?" When he returned home, neighbors and relatives all gathered around, each with a thirst for knowledge and curiosity, to ask A Gen, who had just returned from the land of immortals.

"..." He described the prosperity of Shanghai in flowery language, exaggerating it many times over, making a group of villagers extremely admire it. In particular, A Gen's father sighed and said, "If I could go to Shanghai once in my life, I could die with my eyes closed! Alas, I'm not blessed!"

"What are you saying, Dad? Why don't you come with me for a few days!" A Gen suddenly had a burst of filial piety and resolutely agreed. So, after a few days, he and his father set off together.

On the way, A Gen's father only imagined the situation in Shanghai, and his cheeks couldn't help but show a smile when he thought of the pleasure. But A Gen was very disappointed, regretting that he had brought his father along, because his father was still wearing a tattered cotton-padded coat, the patches on which were stacked like a pagoda. He was afraid that he would be ridiculed in Shanghai and lose his false display of status... but there was nothing he could do, and he often sighed softly.

When they arrived in Shanghai, they went to roam around everywhere. A Gen's friends saw the country bumpkin who came with him and were twelve parts confused, so they quietly asked him, "Who is that person with you? So poor!"

A Gen was really a little embarrassed. After thinking for a few moments, he was considered clever and alert, so he concealed the truth and replied, "Just because his daughter-in-law and I are on good terms, I brought him along to play."

These words made his friends even more confused, so they teased the country bumpkin behind A Gen's back, "Don't look down on this old bumpkin, there is still a flower in his house!"

"What are you talking about? I don't understand!"

"Still pretending! Your daughter-in-law is actually on good terms with Brother A Gen, don't you know that?"

"Oh, you only know one thing, but not the other... You only know that my daughter-in-law and he are on good terms, but you don't know that his mother sleeps with me!"

"..."

"....................................."

Somehow, A Gen heard these words. He knew that the lie had been exposed, so he had to tell the truth. This kind of strange phenomenon is probably endless in today's deformed society. A wealthy stranger may be recognized as parents, uncles, and elders; otherwise, even if they are one's own parents, they are treated as strangers on the road!

Ah, the strange phenomenon of a deformed society! The evil psychology of base people!

Clerk Communication Column Regulations

(1) Communication Purpose: The purpose of this column is to gather wisdom, explain difficult questions, learn from each other, and enhance the happiness of life.

(2) Communication Target: The target of this column, in terms of people, is limited to shop clerks and apprentices, and in terms of location, is limited to this city.

(3) Communication Content: All questions regarding personal daily life such as...

(1) Occupation (2) Moral and academic cultivation (3) Entertainment and sports (4) Marriage, as well as other questions related to the country and society, are welcome. If the content of the question is too profound and beyond the ability of this column, it can also be introduced to this newspaper's "Reader Advisor" for answering.

(4) Method of Sending Letters

(1) The name, age, native place, occupation, and detailed mailing address must be clearly written at the end of the letter. These items must still be clearly written in subsequent letters.

(2) The style of the letter is not limited, but it should be simple and easy to understand, and it must be written clearly.

(3) Please write "Shenbao News, this city, Supplement - Clerk Communication Column" on the letter. If a reply is required, please attach a two-cent stamp.

(4) The sender must cut out the special printed stamp of this column and paste it in the upper left corner of the letter. Letters without stamps will not be answered.

(5) Handling Method After Receiving Letters

(1) If this newspaper believes that the questions discussed have the value of contributing to the public, they may be disclosed in the newspaper.

(2) To respect the opinions of the sender, all letters that state that they do not wish to disclose their name or that require a separate response will be handled accordingly.

(3) If the sender hopes to disclose the letter in the newspaper, but because the length is too long and cannot be fully disclosed, the main points will be published. Also, if the content of the question is complex and requires careful study, resulting in a delayed response or disclosure, please understand.

(4) When there are many letters, the answers will be given according to the order in which they were received. If there are any delays, please understand.

Novel: Writing a Letter to a Friend's Wife (15 Continued) Qin Shouou 180

Therefore, I am often thinking that although I am not a great revolutionary or a national superstar, in the minds of the general intellectual class, there is at least some recognition of me. If I could generously give up everything I have, abandon all the material enjoyment I have before me, and leave alone to join the Volunteer Army in Northeast China, the newspapers would inevitably have several eye-catching reports. (They would not know my true intentions!) Perhaps this could awaken some people, and these awakened people could alert the rest. This would not be in vain for my father who raised me for twenty-five years.

Since the idea of sacrificing myself for the person I love has been decided, I have chosen this method of sacrifice. It is a win-win situation. Although it cannot be said to be "death heavier than Mount Tai," at least it is not as light as Zijin Mountain in Nanjing!

It seems that everything I wanted to say has been said! Some of it is funny and ridiculous, and some of it is passionate and intense. I didn't expect that I, Zhu Jinchi, would have such a great article left behind before I die!

Dear little friend! You may be tired of reading it? But please forgive me. This letter is my last expression to the outside world. After this, if you want to see a word from me or hear a word from me, I am afraid it will not be a fact that can be encountered during the day—perhaps it can still be found in a dream—so I really don't want to end it easily.

Didn't I make a very funny curse just now? I said, "If China does not perish within ten years, I would like to become a tortoise in my next life." This was originally said in jest. Of course, I don't want our Great Republic of China to really perish within ten years, and of course, I don't want to be reincarnated as a little tortoise that will be infamous for ten thousand years—but I can be very frank and sincere in telling you about my direction in the next life. Although the so-called next life is fundamentally a vague and ethereal thing!

I remember the last time I saw you, your belly seemed to be a few points higher than usual. Based on the situation of the previous few days, your and Da Jing's second crystallization is clearly in the process of being manufactured. I further predict that I will leave customs at the end of September and arrive at my destination in mid-October. Based on my physique and combat experience, I will probably have to be listed among the national martyrs before the labor of next year. Then, when the little animal in your belly has grown and is ready to be born, I can catch up in time and drill my soul into his or her body.

If such a thing can really be realized, then my death will be even happier than immortals ascending to heaven after corpse liberation! Beautiful little piglet! I only want to be your son, your daughter, to revolve in your arms all day long, and never let you leave me! I will be more filial than Wang Xiang and Lao Laizi! I don't want a little friend, I don't want a lover, I don't want to marry a wife or marry, I only hope to serve you, this little friend, for life! But please remember—you must never let Da Jing hire a wet nurse for me, otherwise, I would rather starve to death as before!

Haha! I have spoken a long string of nonsense again. At this moment, the car has passed Tangguantun and is about to arrive in Tianjin. When I get to Tianjin, I will hand this letter to the post office. I expect it will be about five days before it reaches you.

The cover of this letter is written very mysteriously. Unless Da Jing has yin and yang in his sleeve, he will never know it. But if you want to let him see it, it doesn't matter. Or it can make him put his mind at ease from now on.

Finished! Everything is finished! Wishing you

Work hard to be your virtuous mother and good wife! Dear little friend, little piglet, little brother! (The End)

A General Outline of the Continental Bank 181

The bank was established in Tianjin in the eighth year of the Republic of China (1919). The main organizers were Mr. Tan and Mr. Sun. The bank had a total capital stock of five million yuan and handled all commercial banking business. It also allocated additional capital to engage in savings and trust services. Subsequently, it established a branch in Beiping. In the ninth year of the Republic of China (1920), it established a branch in Shanghai. Branches and offices were then successively established in Hankou, Nanjing, Suzhou, Wuxi, Hangzhou, Qingdao, Jinan, and other places. In the twelfth year of the Republic of China (1923), it jointly established the Four Banks Savings Society and the Four Banks Reserve with the Yien Yieh, Kincheng, and China & South Sea Banks, operating together and jointly issuing China & South Sea banknotes. The bank's concurrent operation of savings and trust businesses was originally approved by the Ministry of Finance when it was registered. Two years ago, it established a special department, opened a separate storefront on Nanjing Road in Shanghai, and separated the savings department to operate independently at the same time as the trust department. The Continental Emporium, built by the trust department, has now been fully completed. The savings and trust departments moved into the new location on Double Tenth Day (October 10th) of this year. The Shanghai branch was originally located at the corner of Tianjin Road and Henan Road, renting land to build its own building. Now, due to business development, it has purchased two mu of land on the east side of Jiujiang Road and Sichuan Road to construct a ten-story building, which is expected to be completed around April or May of next year and will then be relocated. In addition, land was purchased between North Suzhou Road and Guangfu Road to build a warehouse specifically for storing mortgaged goods. The warehouse is very large and was completed a year ago. Attached are the architectural drawings and descriptions of the bank's three major buildings in Shanghai, as reference material for those in the country who are concerned about new buildings.

The Continental Building is About to be Completed 182

Designed by the Murphy and Dana Architects

Constructed by the Shen Tai Hing Kee Construction Company

The Continental Bank of Shanghai has seen its business flourish for more than ten years since its opening, becoming a leader among Shanghai's banks. The original location at Tianjin Road and Henan Road gradually became insufficient. At the end of the previous year, it purchased a land base at the corner of Jiujiang Road and Sichuan Road to build a building, making every effort to operate. It has been over a year, and it is heard that it will be completed in the coming spring. The building is majestic and magnificent, rarely seen in Shanghai. In addition to being used for business operations, the building has multiple floors upstairs for rent. The entire building is designed and supervised by the Murphy and Dana Architects, assisted by Mr. Luo Bangjie, the bank's architect, who is responsible for handling all matters.

The civil engineering is contracted by the Shen Tai Hing Kee Construction Company. Other projects such as heating, sanitation, electrical wiring, steel windows, and elevators are contracted by well-known manufacturers in Shanghai. Construction officially started in May of last year and is scheduled to be completed in January of the coming year. However, due to the impact of the Shanghai War, it will be completed around May. The total cost is over one million taels.

The overall structure, exterior, and interior are mainly simple and solemn. The layout is modern, and all patterns and clues are implicit and have profound meanings. The architect's original intention was to win with the charm of the layout and the majesty and solemnity of the building.

The building has ten floors. The front is 115 feet high. An additional room is opened on the roof as a bank staff club. The basement floor and the mezzanine floor are for the bank's own use. The vault and machine room occupy most of the basement floor, and the latest type of safe deposit boxes are placed on the mezzanine floor.

All vault doors and safe deposit boxes are specially planned and installed by the American (Mosler) company. Machines are installed that can sound an alarm even if the slightest sound or sound wave occurs in the vault after office hours. The entire building is densely covered with alarm bells for protection, especially for the protection of safe deposit boxes.

There are seven floors available for rent, with a total area of 530,000 square feet. The light in each room is exceptionally sufficient. Each room can be directly accessed from the corridor, but it is also very easy to divide the rooms. Most of the rooms have windows on two sides, allowing for air circulation. Each floor is equipped with water heating and modern sanitary facilities, and each room is also equipped with various electrical and telephone lines for tenants to connect to external lines.

The entire building is equipped with two of the latest Otis elevators, which can rise 500 feet per minute. The upper and lower floors are spacious, so even if there are many tenants going up and down, there will be no crowding.

According to the architect's observation, the upper part of the building can be rented out around mid-February of the coming year. The bank portion will take about three months longer due to the time-consuming marble, bronze, and interior decoration.

The Construction of the Continental Warehouse 183

Blueprint by Tonghe Foreign Firm

Constructed by Shen Tai Hing Kee Construction Company

The Continental Bank Warehouse in Shanghai is located on the west side of the New Rubbish Bridge, on the border of the International Settlement, and faces the Suzhou River, making water and land transportation very convenient. The warehouse is a five-story building designed by Tonghe Foreign Firm. It was fully completed in May of last year. The interior is divided into two warehouses. No. 1114 North Suzhou Road is the first warehouse, and No. 1 Guangfu Road is the second warehouse, covering a total area of over two mu and three fen. As for the engineering aspect, in addition to the walls being built with ten-inch bricks, the entire structure is made of reinforced concrete, making it strong and durable. The drilling and driving were undertaken by the West Public School and Gong Kee Construction Company.

American pine wood, 25 feet long and 12 inches square, with a distance of 3 feet 6 inches around each pile, accounts for almost one-third of the total construction cost, so the foundation is very solid. It can be said to be one of the best among ordinary warehouses, so cargo insurance is also calculated at the lowest rate. The height of each floor is 17 and a half feet for the first floor, 12 and a half feet for the second floor, and 12 feet for the third floor and above. Steel windows are used in the front and back to circulate air, adopting the latest European and American styles. It is also heard that the warehouse staff has scientific experience in storing goods. They can distinguish the arrangement of all kinds of goods, their properties, and their relationship to the climate in detail, and can handle them appropriately by classification. Goods stored in the warehouse can be mortgaged to the bank at any time, which is of great benefit to customers. The warehouse was constructed by Shen Tai Hing Kee Construction Company. When the construction of the Science Museum of the National Qingdao University was in progress, photography was undertaken by Shen Tai Hing Kee Construction Company.

One Aspect of Gong Kee Construction Company's Service to the Country During the Shanghai War 184

The Continental Emporium, constructed by Gong Kee Construction Company, has a total area of over 60,000 square feet and cost over 700,000 yuan. The completion time was only seven and a half months, which is truly remarkable. This is due to the rich engineering experience of the person in charge. When the Japanese invaded Shanghai, the company's project had not yet been completed and handed over. At that time, there was constant gunfire and mourning everywhere. After Mr. Li Denghui and Mr. Zhao Jinqing consulted with the owner, the entire first, second, and third floors of the building were used as a refugee shelter, and the fourth, fifth, and sixth floors were used as a women's wounded soldier hospital. All the walls, doors, windows, floors, paint, etc., were damaged and dirtied. The company voluntarily repaired them completely. All water and electricity were supplied by the company at that time, which was also quite costly. This is sufficient to prove that the company is well-managed and spares no effort to serve the country. The projects undertaken by the company include the six-story building of Renji Hospital on Shandong Road, the church opposite the Municipal Council, and the West Public School. The achievements are outstanding, and all owners and architects who have entrusted the company to undertake projects are satisfied and are often in the industry as well.

A Brief Biography of Architect Zhao Shen 185

Architect Zhao Shen, courtesy name Yuanru, is a native of Wuxi, Jiangsu. He is 34 years old this year. After graduating from Tsinghua University in 1919, he entered Ben Xue Wen Yi University in the United States. In 1922, he obtained a Bachelor of Science degree in architecture. The following year, he obtained a Master of Architecture degree. After that, he stayed in the United States for three years, working as a design technician in a well-known architectural firm, responsible for designing several large projects. For example, in 1923, he designed the 20-story building of the New York Baohuali Savings Bank, costing 10 million US dollars. In 1924, he designed the 34-story building of the Bi Labaobao University, costing 20 million US dollars. In the same year, he designed the St. Louis Research Institute, costing 5 million US dollars, as well as the Chicago Review newspaper office and other large buildings. In 1926, he left the United States and traveled around Europe for a year, viewing all the famous buildings of various dynasties in various countries. He returned to China in 1927 and served as the director of the architectural department of the Shanghai Qingdao Association. The following year, he jointly established an architectural firm with Mr. Fan Wenzhao. In 1930, Jun reorganized the Zhao Shen Architectural Firm. The following year, architects Chen Zhi and Tong Wo joined the current joint firm at No. 40 Ningbo Road, 4th floor. Major buildings designed by Jun in Shanghai and Nanjing include the West YMCA, Nanyang Grand Theater, new dormitory of Jiaotong University, naval hospital of Jiangnan Shipyard, Xihai Grand Theater, Lianzhu Building, Hengli Bank Building, Da Shanghai Theater, and the new building of Zhejiang Industrial Bank in this area. In Nanjing, there are the Ministry of Railways, Lizhi Society, Overseas Chinese Guest House, new building of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, the residence of Minister Kong of Junyuan, and the memorial pavilion of the Mausoleum. In 1925, he won the first honorary prize for the design of the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-sen in Nanjing. In 1930, he won the first prize for the design of the new municipal government building in the city center. In the same year, he also won the first prize for the design of the Mausoleum of Dr. Sun Yat-sen Memorial Tower in Nanjing. Jun is a member of the American Institute of Architects, a member of the Chinese Institute of Architects, a registered architect of the Ministry of Industry, and a member of the Shanghai United Youth Society and the Nanjing International Social Club. He is currently the president of the Chinese Institute of Architects.

Special Architectural Issue

The Origin of the Continental Bank Trust Department's Construction of the Continental Emporium 186

Shanghai has become China's leading modern metropolis. Its trade and industrial and commercial prosperity also rank sixth among the world's major cities. This is something everyone knows. However, if we examine it carefully, although we see that Shanghai's area is so vast, the prosperous center is probably only a few miles in radius. Just imagine that in this area of only a few miles, countless Chinese and foreign, old and new industrial and commercial enterprises are gathered. In fact, it is very crowded and compact, making it extremely difficult. Therefore, they push and squeeze each other, and even occupy and seize each other. Those with stronger financial resources can barely obtain an inch of land, while those with weaker financial resources can only be excluded from the city. Now, how many large factories and large stores cannot develop their businesses, and eventually fail or even lose money because they cannot obtain a central location to display samples or set up business offices. It is truly regrettable to see. Is it because they lack capital, talent, or have poor products?

The success of a prosperous central urban area cannot be achieved overnight, by one person or one force. It has its own situation and history. Since Shanghai's prosperous center is so narrow, to solve this urgent need, we must think of a special method. The Continental Bank Trust Department of Shanghai, with its dedication to serving society and its mission of assisting industry and commerce, has keenly realized this major shortcoming. Especially the pain felt by our country's backward industry and commerce is even more profound, so it must be resolved immediately. Therefore, there was a motion to establish this Continental Emporium. After a long period of research and discussion, it was found that selecting a site was the most difficult. Later, based on the situation of modern business in Shanghai and the trend of future development, a large piece of land was surveyed and determined to be the site for building the emporium, bordering Nanjing Road to the north, Shandong Road to the east, Jiujiang Road to the south, and Youxin Street to the west. As for the superiority of this location, the importance of the situation, and the convenience of transportation, it can indeed be counted as one of the best in the prosperous center of Shanghai. It is very close to the Huangpu River in the east, and it is close to the Huajinli (Shanxi Road) and Rishenglou (Zhejiang Road) areas in the west. It is not far from the French Concession in the south, and it is very convenient to go to the railway station and Hongkou in the north. Therefore, it has become a thoroughfare for the whole city and a trade passage. Moreover, the area capacity is also very large, with more than nine mu of land. It is most suitable to build a great and magnificent emporium in this great location. However, although the landlord is Hartong Foreign Firm, the Continental Trust Department has already had a long-term plan and has signed a long-term lease (32 years).

The Continental Building Under Construction, Designed by Murphy and Dana Architects, Constructed by Shen Tai Hing Kee Construction Company

Designed by Architect Zhuang Jun

Constructed by Gong Kee Construction Company

After determining the site, the Continental Trust Department entrusted Mr. Zhuang Jun, a famous architect in Shanghai, to design the blueprint in the spring of the 20th year of the Republic of China (1931). Mr. Zhuang referred to the latest plans from various countries in the world as a standard and supplemented them with modern needs and our country's habits. Mr. Zhuang had very deep experience and quickly completed the plan for this great building. At the same time, Gong Kee Construction Company of this city won the bid to undertake the construction at a cost of more than 700,000 yuan. On March 19th of the same year, the ceremony for the auspicious start of construction was held. Originally, it was expected that the entire building could be handed over in seven and a half months, but unfortunately the Shanghai War broke out, and therefore, it was suspended for several months in the middle. Later, after the agreement was signed and society returned to its original state, Gong Kee Construction Company immediately completed its unfinished construction. By the National Day of this year, this unprecedented grand emporium in Shanghai was finally able to meet us. Looking at the construction of such a large building, the total time required was only a few months. It is truly admirable for the greatness and speed of Gong Kee Construction Company.

The General Aspect of the House and

The Past and Present of Hotel Lanes

According to the building permits issued by the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council, the construction of the Continental Emporium is the largest. Therefore, the vast area of this emporium and the magnificent construction of the entire building are undoubtedly one of the best in modern Shanghai. Moreover, the four sides of the foundation are all adjacent to major roads. The central part facing Nanjing Road has eight floors, and both sides also have seven floors. A towering tower is built at the corner of Shandong Road, with nine floors, soaring into the clouds, which is also the highest peak of the entire building. The side along Jiujiang Road is four stories high. The entire building was designed by concrete engineer Mr. Miao Kaibo and built into an extremely solid skeleton. Therefore, in addition to being solemn and magnificent, it is very solid. It is specially equipped with all steel windows undertaken by the Shanghai East Asia and Shanghai Er Steel Window Companies. Looking at it, it naturally feels more excellent and beautiful.
